approved contingency amount.
CEQA: This Project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation,
repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures,
facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or
former use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)

11.
Clean Water Program Labor Compliance Consultant – Amendment
Approve Amendment No. 2 to the agreement with TSG Enterprises, Inc. DBA The Solis Group for on-call labor
compliance services for the Clean Water Program in an amount not to exceed $50,000, for a total amount of
$450,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the amendment in substantially the form
presented.
CEQA: The City prepared a Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR) in accordance with the
California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) (SCH No. 2015032006). The PEIR was certified by City Council on June
6, 2016. In accordance with CEQA, the Final PEIR serves as the primary environmental compliance document for
implementation of the Clean Water Program. The City prepared an Addendum to the Final PEIR that were
approved on July 16, 2018 (Addendum 1) and April 15, 2019 (Addendum 2). This work is within the scope of the
project evaluated in the PEIR and Addenda.

PUBLIC COMMENT
Members of the public wishing to comment on any item not appearing on the agenda may address the City Council at this time. State
law prevents Council from taking action on any matter not on the agenda; your comments may be referred to staff for follow up.
Public comment is limited to a total of 15 minutes; however, an opportunity for additional public comment may be provided later in
the agenda.
 
PUBLIC HEARING
City Council action on the following public hearing(s) represents a final decision concluding all administrative proceedings. Judicial
review may be had only if a petition is filed with the Court not later than the 90th day following the date the decision is made.
Judicial review of environmental determinations may be subject to a time period for litigation as short as 30 days following the date
the decision is made.
 
13.
2033 La Salle Drive - Zoning Reclassification, Zoning Code Amendment, and Planning Application for an Early
Childhood Education Center – Ordinance Introduction
Introduce an Ordinance to approve a Zoning Reclassification from R1-B to R1-B/Q8, and a Zoning Code
Amendment to provide development standards for an educational facility and find it exempt from CEQA pursuant
to Section 15061(b)(3) (Common Sense Exemption); and adopt a Resolution to approve the Planning Application
(Special Use Permit, Site Plan and Architectural Review and Site Development Planning Application) for the
development of an Early Childhood Education Center subject to the findings for approval and conditions of
approval, and find it exempt from CEQA pursuant to Section 15303 (New Small Structures Exemption).
CEQA: The Zoning Reclassification and Zoning Map Amendment are exempt from the California Environmental
Quality Act (CEQA) pursuant to the Common Sense Exemption (CEQA Guidelines, 14 CCR Section 15061(b)(3)). The
development of the Project itself is categorically exempt from CEQA pursuant to CEQA Guidelines Section 15303
(Class 3), New Construction or Conversion of Small Structures.

PUBLIC COMMENTS/REQUEST TO SPEAK
Prior to the Meeting 
Send comments to: clerk@cityofsanmateo.org until 4 p.m. the day of the meeting.
During the meeting
By Zoom: Click the link at the top of the agenda and you’ll be added to the meeting. All attendees are muted by default. When the item of interest
is open for consideration, select the “Raise Your Hand” icon and you will be called on at the appropriate time.
By telephone: Call (408) 638-0968 and enter the conference ID found at the top of the meeting agenda. When the item of interest is open for
consideration, select *9 to raise your hand. When called upon, press *6 to unmute, state your name and provide your comments.
In Person: At the meeting complete a “Request to Speak” form. Organized Group and Presentations: Up to five (5) minutes for a group presentation,
with as many speakers as can be accommodated within that time allowance. To qualify for a group presentation, all individuals associated with the
presentation must be clearly identified and confirmed as in attendance at the meeting. Presentation materials must be submitted to
clerk@cityofsanmateo.org one (1) business day in advance of the meeting.
ACCESSIBILITY: In compliance with the Americans with Disabilities Act and to ensure meaningful access for all participants, including those with
limited English proficiency, individuals requiring special accommodations or language assistance to participate in this meeting may contact the City
Clerk’s Office at (650) 522-7040 or clerk@cityofsanmateo.org . Notification 48 hours prior to the meeting will enable the City to make reasonable
arrangements to ensure accessibility to this meeting.

SUBJECT:
City Council 2026 Regular Meeting Calendar — Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt an amendment to the City Council Regular Meeting schedule for the calendar year 2026 to move the first meeting in 
October to Monday, October 5, 2026.
BACKGROUND:
On October 6, 2025, the City Council adopted a proposed calendar of regular meetings for calendar year 2026. As part of 
that action, the first October meeting was scheduled for Wednesday, October 7, due to an anticipated holiday conflict. 
Since that time, the conflict has been resolved. Accordingly, staff is recommending that the October meetings return to the 
City Council’s standard meeting schedule of the first and third Monday of the month.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budgetary impact associated with this administrative item. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result in 
direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

SUBJECT:
Fiscal Year 2025-26 Wastewater Treatment Plant Property Insurance — Purchase Authorization
RECOMMENDATION:
Authorize the City Attorney to purchase property insurance for the Wastewater Treatment Plant for the remainder of fiscal 
year 2025-26, in an amount not to exceed $237,394.02.
BACKGROUND:
The City is presently enrolled in an organization called Public Risk Innovations, Solutions, and Management (PRISM), 
formerly known as the California State Association of Counties (CSAC) Excess Insurance Authority. PRISM is a joint powers 
authority comprised of dozens of government agencies that provides coverage up to $25 million above a $1 million Self-
Insured Retention (SIR) per occurrence, and a $1 million Individual Member Corridor Deductible (IMCD) that erodes over 
the course of the fiscal year in exchange for a premium discount for the excess liability insurance policy. 
For the past five years, the City Council has authorized a staff committee comprised of the City Manager, the Finance 
Director, and the City Attorney to select the most cost-effective program to insure the City’s general liability and property 
risks and authorized the City Attorney to execute all required documents to purchase the selected insurance. Most 
recently, on June 16, 2025, the City Council authorized the selection of such insurance for fiscal year 2025-26. 
The Wastewater Treatment Plant (WWTP) was until recently covered by a builder’s risk insurance policy during the period 
of construction. With construction nearing final completion, coverage for the WWTP was transferred to the City’s 
Property, Boiler & Machinery, Environmental & Cyber (APIP) insurance policy on December 17, 2025. 
This transfer requires an additional insurance premium payment in the amount of $237,393.02 for the remainder of fiscal 
year 2025-26. 
The APIP premium for the current fiscal year is $1,099,777. While the City Council authorization on June 16, 2025 provided 
broad authority to select and purchase insurance, given the significant additional premium for the WWTP, staff is seeking 
specific authority for this payment in an abundance of caution. 
For fiscal year 2026-27, the APIP insurance policy premium for the WWTP is currently estimated at $406,804.02. This will 
be accounted for in a forthcoming staff report seeking authority to select and purchase insurance for fiscal year 2026-27, 
most likely in June 2026.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The fiscal year 2025-26 budget accounted for $4.1 million for insurance premiums. Insurance premium payments in the 
amount of $3.5 million were made, leaving a balance of $600k which is sufficient for the proposed payment of 
8 of 409

--- page 9 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
$237,394.02. Therefore, no modifications to appropriations are required.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This item is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not cause a physical change in 
the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)

All meeting noticing requirements were met.

SUBJECT:
Ballot Measure Communications Consulting Services for the November 2026 General Election — Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with TeamCivX for ballot measure communications consulting services in the amount of $174,000 
and authorize the City Manager to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
Ballot Measure Subcommittee Recommendation 
The City hired True North Research to conduct polling services regarding a potential City revenue measure on the 
November 2026 ballot. Staff worked with True North Research to design and conduct a study that provides the City of San 
Mateo with a statistically reliable understanding of voters’ interest in funding priority repairs and improvements to the 
City’s infrastructure systems as well as general municipal services with a local revenue measure (bond or sales tax). On 
January 7, 2026, staff met with the City Council Revenue Measure Ad Hoc Committee. Based on the poll results, the Ad 
Hoc Committee recommends that City staff continue pursuing the feasibility of a sales tax measure. If passed, the sales tax 
measure would result in approximately $7 million annually in new revenue to help address the City's structural budget 
deficit. 
Consultant 
The City conducted a RFP process to find the best ballot measure communications consultant available. TeamCivX 
submitted a strong proposal. During the last three election cycles, the City contracted with TeamCivX (previously part of 
TBWBH Props and Measures) to assist with providing neutral, public information on ballot measures consistent with state 
law. TeamCivX’s scope of services include deliverables around community outreach, feedback and awareness building 
along with assisting with the development of draft ballot measure language. The full list of deliverables can be found in 
Attachment 1 under scope of services. 
Due to the positive past experiences with TeamCivX, and their proposal and interview, staff is recommending that the City 
Council approve a contract with TeamCivX. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
The not to exceed amount for this agreement is $174,000. The City Manager's Office's Professional Services budget has the 
funds available for the agreement. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This item is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not cause a physical change in 
the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)

AGREEMENT WITH TEAMCIVX
FOR PROFESSIONAL CONSULTANT SERVICES
FOR 
BALLOT MEASURE COMMUNICATIONS CONSULTING SERVICES
This Agreement, made and entered into this day of _____________, by and between the CITY 
OF SAN MATEO, a municipal corporation existing under the laws of the State of California (“CITY”), and 
TeamCivX, a limited liability company (“CONSULTANT”), whose address is 21 Orinda Way, Suite C-191, 
Orinda, CA 94563.
RECITALS:
A.  CITY desires certain to assess the electoral feasibility of a ballot measure, and help 
educate and inform the community about the proposed ballot measure hereinafter described.
B.  CITY desires to engage CONSULTANT to provide these communications services by 
reason of its qualifications and experience for performing such services and CONSULTANT has offered 
to provide the required services on the terms and in the manner set forth herein.
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS AGREED as follows:
SECTION 1 - SCOPE OF SERVICES
The scope of services to be performed by CONSULTANT under this Agreement is as described in 
Exhibit A to this Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
SECTION 2 - DUTIES OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for the professional quality, technical accuracy and 
coordination of all work furnished by CONSULTANT under this Agreement.  CONSULTANT shall, without 
additional compensation, correct or revise any errors or deficiencies in its work.
CONSULTANT represents that it is qualified to furnish the services described under this 
Agreement.
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for employing or engaging all persons necessary to perform 
the services of CONSULTANT.
CONSULTANT agrees to comply with the City’s minimum wage ordinance as codified in 
Municipal Code Chapter 5.92, which differs from the state minimum wage and includes a Consumer 
Price Index escalator.
SECTION 3 - DUTIES OF CITY
CITY shall provide pertinent information regarding its requirements for the project.
12 of 409

--- page 13 ---
Professional Consultant Services
Page 2 of 12
Rev 5/25
CITY shall examine documents submitted by CONSULTANT and shall render decisions pertaining 
thereto promptly, to avoid unreasonable delay in the progress of CONSULTANT's work.
SECTION 4 - TERM
The services to be performed under this Agreement shall commence on February 1, 2026 and 
be completed on July 31, 2026.
SECTION 5 - PAYMENT
Payment shall be made by CITY only for services rendered and upon submission of a payment 
request upon completion and CITY approval of the work performed.  In consideration for the full 
performance of the services set forth in Exhibit A, CITY agrees to pay CONSULTANT a fee in an amount 
of $174,000, pursuant to rates stated in Exhibit B to this Agreement, attached and incorporated by 
reference.
SECTION 6 - TERMINATION
Without limitation to such rights or remedies as CITY shall otherwise have by law, CITY shall have 
the right to terminate this Agreement or suspend work on the Project for any reason, upon ten (10) days' 
written notice to CONSULTANT.  CONSULTANT agrees to cease all work under this Agreement upon 
receipt of said written notice.
Upon termination and upon CITY's payment of the amount required to be paid, documents 
become the property of CITY, and CONSULTANT shall transfer them to CITY upon request without 
additional compensation.
SECTION 7 - OWNERSHIP OF DOCUMENTS
All documents prepared by CONSULTANT in the performance of this Agreement, although 
instruments of professional service, are and shall be the property of CITY, whether the project for 
which they are made is executed or not.
SECTION 8 - CONFIDENTIALITY
All reports and documents prepared by CONSULTANT in connection with the performance of 
this Agreement are confidential until released by CITY to the public.  CONSULTANT shall not make any 
such documents or information available to any individual or organization not employed by 
CONSULTANT or CITY without the written consent of CITY before any such release.
SECTION 9 - INTEREST OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT covenants that it presently has no interest, and shall not acquire any interest, 
direct or indirect, financial or otherwise, which would conflict in any manner or degree with the 
performance of the services under this Agreement.

SECTION 10 - CONSULTANT'S STATUS
It is expressly agreed that in the performance of the professional services required under this 
Agreement, CONSULTANT shall at all times be considered an independent contractor as defined in 
Labor Code Section 3353, under control of the CITY as to the result of the work but not the means by 
which the result is accomplished.  Nothing herein shall be construed to make CONSULTANT an agent or 
employee of CITY while providing services under this Agreement.
SECTION 11 - INDEMNITY
CONSULTANT agrees to hold harmless and indemnify CITY, its elected and appointed officials, 
employees, and agents from and against any and all claims, loss, liability, damage, and expense arising 
out of CONSULTANT’s negligent performance of this Agreement, except those claims arising out of 
CITY’s sole negligence or willful misconduct.  CONSULTANT agrees to defend City, its elected and 
appointed officials, employees, and agents against any such claims. The CONSULTANT’S duty to 
indemnify shall survive expiration or early termination of this Agreement.
SECTION 12 - INSURANCE
CONSULTANT shall procure and maintain for the duration of the contract and three years 
thereafter (five years for building or major improvements) the insurance specified in Exhibit C to this 
Agreement.
SECTION 13 - NON-ASSIGNABILITY
Both parties hereto recognize that this Agreement is for the personal services of CONSULTANT 
and cannot be transferred, assigned, or subcontracted by CONSULTANT without the prior written 
consent of CITY.
SECTION 14 - RELIANCE UPON PROFESSIONAL
SKILL OF CONSULTANT
It is mutually understood and agreed by and between the parties hereto that CONSULTANT is 
skilled in the professional calling necessary to perform the work agreed to be done under this 
Agreement and that CITY relies upon the skill of CONSULTANT to do and perform the work in the most 
skillful manner, and CONSULTANT agrees to thus perform the work.  The acceptance of CONSULTANT's 
work by CITY does not operate as a release of CONSULTANT from said obligation.

SECTION 15 - WAIVERS
The waiver by either party of any breach or violation of any term, covenant, or condition of this 
Agreement or of any provisions of any ordinance or law shall not be deemed to be a waiver of such 
term, covenant, condition, ordinance or law or of any subsequent breach or violation of the same or of 
any other term, condition, ordinance, or law.  The subsequent acceptance by either party of any fee or 
other money which may become due hereunder shall not be deemed to be a waiver of any preceding 
breach or violation by the other party of any term, covenant, or condition of this Agreement or of any 
applicable law or ordinance.
SECTION 16 - SEVERABILITY
If any term or portion of this Agreement is held to be invalid, illegal, or otherwise 
unenforceable by a court of competent jurisdiction, the remaining provisions of this Agreement shall 
continue in full force and effect.
SECTION 17 - COSTS AND ATTORNEY FEES
Attorney fees in total amount not exceeding $5000, shall be recoverable as costs (by the filing 
of a cost bill) by the prevailing party in any action or actions to enforce the provisions of this 
Agreement.  The above $5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court, 
appellate court, or otherwise, and regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions.  It 
is the intent of this Agreement that neither party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for 
attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to enforce the provisions of this Agreement.
SECTION 18 - NON-DISCRIMINATION
CONSULTANT warrants that it is an Equal Opportunity Employer and shall comply with 
applicable regulations governing equal employment opportunity.  Neither CONSULTANT nor any of its 
subcontractors shall discriminate in the employment of any person because of race, color, national 
origin, ancestry, physical handicap, medical condition, marital status, sex, or age, unless based upon a 
bona fide occupational qualification pursuant to the California Fair Employment and Housing Act.
SECTION 19 - MEDIATION
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to 
mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be 
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one 
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
Feasibility Assessment/Messaging 
A.
Deep-dive review of the February 2025 True North Research community opinion 
survey, past ballot measure data and polls, current and historical City policy documents and 
video recordings of relevant City Council meetings/discussions to understand the issues under 
consideration;
B.
Develop education and information approaches to the potential ballot measure 
based on polling data completed by polling consultant;
C.
Assist City staff with informational messaging needs related to the potential 
ballot measures (ongoing). Oversee translation of materials into Spanish; 
D.
Collaborate with polling consultant to design, conduct and analyze a follow-up 
poll (Spring 2026) of voters in the City of San Mateo to assess the feasibility of a ballot 
measure;
E.
Analyze past election results in the City and region to understand voter turnout 
trends and other relevant voting patterns;
F.
Research other local, regional and state ballot measures that may be heading to 
an upcoming ballot that could compete with City’s ballot measure(s); 
G.
Make specific recommendations regarding 1) the ballot measure type that best 
reflects the priorities of San Mateo residents, and 2) other important ballot measure features; 
and
H.
Review/edit/make recommendations regarding City-drafted press releases and 
other project-related City communications.
Ballot Measure Development:
A.
Work with legal counsel and polling consultant to develop the 75-word ballot 
question;
B.
Work with the City Clerk’s Office to make sure all steps are taken to have measure 
placed on the November 2026 ballot;
C.
Work with legal counsel and polling consultant to develop and refine the full text 
of ballot measure and other materials that will appear in the ballot pamphlet mailed to all 
voters; 
21 of 409

--- page 22 ---
Professional Consultant Services
Page 9 of 12
Rev 5/25
D.
Present recommendations, documents and resolutions to the City Council or City 
Council Subcommittee; and
E.
In coordination with the polling consultant, develop a recommended timeline 
and calendar from contract start date through July 2026.
Public Information to Raise Awareness and Educate and Inform of the Potential Ballot Measure:
A.
Develop informational messaging and fact sheets to be distributed at community 
meetings and events;
B.
Provide talking points, frequently asked questions, and message training for staff;
C.
Provide content related to proposed ballot measure to be added to City’s 
website, used in social media, included in email updates and added to newsletters;
D.
Prepare PowerPoint presentations for public and community meetings;
E.
Write, design, and produce mailings and advertising to inform residents; 
F.
Develop plans to inform internal stakeholder groups, including commissions, 
staff, employee groups, and others; and
G.
Develop plans to inform external groups including elected leaders, business 
leaders, ethnic community leaders, faith community leaders, neighborhood groups and others.

EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate.
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.
Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City.

SUBJECT:
San Mateo City Employees’ Association Side Letter of Agreement Regarding Retirement Health Savings Account – Approval
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to amend the Memorandum of Understanding (”MOU”) with the San Mateo City Employees’ 
Association (”SMCEA”) to modify the terms of Section 24.11 Retirement Health Savings Account. 
BACKGROUND:
The purpose of this side letter of agreement is to change the conversion of separation pay arrangements regarding the 
Retirement Health Savings Account for calendar year 2026 as agreed upon by the City and SMCEA. 
All employee separations (service or disability retirement) occurring between January 1, 2026 and December 31, 2026 shall 
be handled in the following manner: 
•
Employees with less than 11 years and 3 months of service shall have all eligible accrued sick leave contributed to 
RHSA, and all other eligible accrued leaves shall be in cash. 
•
Employees with more than 11 years and 3 months of service to less than 19 years and 11 months of service shall 
have 100% of all eligible accrued leaves paid out in cash. 
•
Employees with more than 19 years and 11 months of service to less than 20 years and 6 months of service shall 
have 100% of all eligible accrued leaves contributed to their Retirement Health Savings Account. 
•
Employees with more than 20 years and 6 months of service to less than 21 years and 6 months of service shall 
have 100% of all eligible accrued leaves shall be paid out in cash. 
•
Employees with more than 21 years and 6 months of service to under 25 years of service shall have all eligible 
accrued sick leave contributed to RHSA, and all other eligible accrued leaves shall be in cash. 
•
Employees with more than 25 years of service to less than 26 years and 10 months of service shall have 100% of all 
eligible accrued leaves contributed to their Retirement Health Savings Account.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The recommended changes for the San Mateo City Employees’ Association (SMCEA) Memorandum of Understanding 
(MOU) do not have a quantifiable fiscal impact.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This Side Letter of Agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is a government fiscal activity which does not 
involve any commitment to any specific project which may result in a potentially significant physical impact on the 
environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

SUBJECT:
San Mateo Management Employees’ Association Side Letter of Agreement Regarding the Retirement Health Savings

RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to amend the Memorandum of Understanding (”MOU”) with the San Mateo Management Employees’ 
Association (”SMMEA”) to modify the terms of Section 26.5- Retirement Health Savings Account. 
BACKGROUND:
The purpose of this side letter of agreement is to change the conversion of separation pay arrangements regarding the 
Retirement Health Savings Account for calendar year 2026 as agreed upon by the City and SMMEA. 
All employee separations (service or disability retirement) from the City occurring between January 1, 2026, and December 
31, 2026, shall be handled in the following manner: 
•
For employees with 41 years or less of merit service credit, all eligible leave balances and eligible sick leave 
balances shall be contributed to the employee's RHSA. 
•
For employees with more than 41 years of merit service credit, 100% of all eligible accrued sick leave balances 
shall be contributed to the employee's RHSA. All other eligible leave balances shall be paid the straight time salary 
equivalent for all accrued leave earned.
•
At the time of non-retirement separation from City merit employment, employees shall contribute no accrued 
leave to his/her RHSA.

Side Letter of Agreement 
Between the San Mateo Management Employees Association and the City of San Mateo 
 
The Memorandum of Understanding (MOU) between the San Mateo Management Employees Association 
("Association") and the City of San Mateo ("City") is set to expire as of 11:59 p.m., April 22, 2028. 
 
MOU Section 26.5 Retirement Health Savings Account states that the Association may elect to change the 
conversion of separation pay arrangement for each successive calendar year of the Agreement. 
 
The Association has elected to change the conversion of separation pay arrangement for calendar year 
2026. All employee separations occurring between January 1, 2026 and December 31, 2026 shall be 
handled in the following manner: 
 
• 
At the time of service or disability retirement from City merit employment, separation pay 
arrangements shall be as follows: 
o 
For employees with 41 years or less of merit service credit, all eligible leave balances and 
eligible sick leave balances shall be contributed to the employee's RHSA 
o 
For employees with more than 41 years of merit service credit, 100% of all eligible accrued 
sick leave balances shall be contributed to the employee's RHSA. All other eligible leave 
balances shall be paid the straight time salary equivalent for all accrued leave earned. 
• 
At the time of non-retirement separation from City merit employment, employees shall contribute 
no accrued leave to his/her RHSA. 
 
For purposes of this Side Letter of Agreement, “eligible sick leave balances” is defined as fifty (50%) of an 
employee’s accrued sick leave up to a maximum of four hundred eighty (480) hours payment.  And all 
other “eligible leave balances” includes vacation, executive, holiday and compensation time. 
 
The Association may elect to change the above conversion of separation pay arrangement for each 
successive calendar year of this Agreement. The Association must notify the City's Human Resources 
Department in writing no later than November 30th of the change(s) to be made for the following calendar 
year. In the event notification is not received by the deadline, the separation pay arrangement in effect at 
the time will continue for the following calendar year. 
 
During the term of this MOU, employees in this bargaining unit may elect to contribute a set amount of 
salary to the RHSA. The City shall be notified of any such election sixty (60) days prior to the effective 
date.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
Agenda Report

Agenda Number:  7
Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR
Account Number: 10-2311
File ID: 25-10766
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Alex Khojikian, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Human Resources Department
MEETING DATE:
January 12, 2026 
SUBJECT:
Updates to Principal and Senior Transportation Planner Job Specs and Senior Planner Salary Schedule — Approval
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve the updated Senior Transportation Planner “Senior” and Principal Transportation Planner 
“Principal” job specification series and the salary range for the new classification of Senior Transportation Planner.
BACKGROUND:
Currently, there is a significant gap between the Associate Transportation Planner and the Principal classifications. The 
Public Works Department is seeking to create a Senior Transportation Planner classification as part of the management 
series to close this gap. The Senior classification will be flexibly staffed to the Principal classification through a competitive 
process. Making these changes will increase flexibility and employee development/potential, create internal promotional 
opportunities for current City employees, and/or attract new talent. The Human Resources Department recommends 
setting the monthly salary range for the Senior Transportation Planner at $10,448.33 – 12,453.76 (10% above the 
Associate Transportation Planner). These changes are being proposed to: 1) update the duties, distinguishing features, and 
qualifications, and 2) add the Senior Transportation Planner to the Transportation Planner series to create a flexibility 
staffed classification. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no fiscal impact as there is sufficient funding within the current budget to support these classifications. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This job specification update is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is a government fiscal activity which does not 
involve any commitment to any specific project which may result in a potentially significant physical impact on the 
environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
ATTACHMENTS
Att 1 – Proposed Resolution
             Exhibit A – Job Specification Principal/Senior Transportation Planner
             Exhibit B – Merit Salary Schedule
Att 2 – Job Specification with tracked changes

JOB SPECIFICATION UPDATES 
DEPARTMENT OF PUBLIC WORKS 
 
WHEREAS, pursuant to the San Mateo Municipal Code Section 2.57.030(d), approval of new 
classifications and related job specifications, salary schedules, compensation changes, elimination or 
reinstatement of positions, reallocation of positions, reclassifications, and revisions of job specifications must be 
approved by City Council Resolution; and 
WHEREAS, the proposed change as detailed below is in response to the Public Works Department’s 
request to create a Senior Transportation Planner “Senior” classification as part of the management series to 
close a significant gap between the Associate Transportation Planner and the Principal classifications “Principal”. 
The Senior classification will be flexibly staffed to the Principal classification through a competitive process. 
Making these changes will increase flexibility and employee development/potential, create internal promotional 
opportunities for current City employees, and/or attract new talent; and 
WHEREAS, the job specifications for the Senior Transportation Planner/Principal Transportation Planner 
were updated to reflect an accurate job scope which is in alignment with the updated job specification which is 
attached hereto as Exhibit A; and 
WHEREAS, the employee association representing the impacted classifications has been informed of the 
job specifications’ updates and has not brought forth any objections or concerns. 
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY RESOLVES 
that: 
1. The revisions to the job specifications for the job specification of Principal Transportation Planner and 
Senior Transportation Planner are not subject to CEQA because it can be seen with certainty that they will not 
cause a physical change in the environment. 
2. The revised job specifications for the classification series, Principal Transportation Planner and Senior 
Transportation Planner are approved and attached as Exhibits A. 
3. The salary schedule for the classification of Senior Transportation Planner is approved and attached 
hereto as Exhibit B.

Exhibit A 
 
 
PRINICPAL TRANSPORTATION PLANNER 
SENIOR TRANSPORTATION PLANNER 
 
 
DEFINITION 
 
Under general direction, organizes, reviews, and participates in transportation planning work; 
supervises the work of professional and technical transportation planning personnel, projects, 
and other activities; and performs other related work as required. 
 
DISTINGUISING CHARACTHERISTICS 
 
Senior Transportation Planner: The Senior Transportation Planner is the first-level supervisor 
in the transportation series. This class is distinguished from the next lower class of Associate 
Transportation Planner by its supervisory duties, when assigned, and by the performance of more 
complex tasks and assignments. This classification supports the development and implementation 
of transportation policies and programs and completes assignments within established 
frameworks. 
 
Principal Transportation Planner: The Principal Transportation Planner is a second-level 
supervisor in the transportation series. This class handles complex, specialized assignments 
with a broad scope.  This classification manages and supervises major transportation programs 
and staff; has a high degree of independent judgment; is expected to lead with minimal 
oversight; leads and manages transportation planning, design activities and program 
integration and evaluation; develops and oversees policies, programs, and projects; and 
manages major transportation initiatives. 
 
The Principal Transportation Planner is a flexibly staffed classification and may be filled by 
advancement from the Senior Transportation Planner classification through a competitive 
process.  
 
SUPERVISION RECEIVED AND EXERCISED 
 
Senior Transportation Planner 
 
Receives oversight and general direction from the Principal Transportation Planner or 
Engineering Manager in the Public Works Department.  
 
Exercises direct supervision over professional, technical, administrative, and other planning 
staff as assigned.  
 
40 of 409

--- page 41 ---
Principal Transportation Planner 
 
Receives oversight and general direction from the Engineering Manager or Deputy Director in 
the Public Works Department.  
 
Exercises direct supervision over professional, technical, administrative, and other planning 
staff as assigned.  
 
EXAMPLES OF DUTIES – Depending on assignment, duties may include, but are not 
limited to, the following: 
 
Senior Transportation Planner 
Supervises professional and technical staff, including prioritizing and assigning work, 
conducting performance evaluations, training staff, and supporting hiring decisions in 
consultation with the Engineering Manager, Deputy Director, and Department Head. 
 
Represents the City and department in communications and interactions, including 
coordination, briefings, and presentations, with other City departments, City Commissions and 
City Council, government agencies, local industries, businesses, community groups, and other 
stakeholders interested in regional and local transportation, transit, traffic, and parking issues. 
 
Plans, coordinates, formulates, and implements, in coordination with other City departments, 
goals, objectives, policies and priorities; and makes recommendations for changes to codes, 
plans and policies, as it relates to transportation planning and parking management.  
 
Directs, coordinates, reviews, and participates in the work of professional, technical, and 
clerical staff, as well as consultants, in data collection, analysis, plan and policy formulation, 
and implementation of a wide variety of projects. 
 
Participates in and provides technical expertise in transportation demand management and 
traffic forecasting including the formulation of a City-wide traffic model and the maintenance 
and update thereof. 
 
Manages administration of the City’s parking permit programs, oversees the collection, 
control, and reconciliation of parking revenues, assists in the preparation and administration of 
the parking program operating budget, monitors expenses, and prudently allocates resources to 
support parking program operations and objectives. 
 
Assists, contributes and manages the planning, design, and construction of capital projects 
including preparation of purchase requisitions, requests for proposals, development of the 
scope of work, professional service agreements and coordination with other City departments 
as appropriate. 
 
41 of 409

--- page 42 ---
Reviews planning applications and building permits in relation to transportation and parking 
related issues, including review of traffic impact analyses, vehicle miles traveled (VMT) 
analyses, and other related transportation studies.  
 
Attend in-person meetings, site visits, and stakeholder engagements, often with minimal 
notice; respond promptly to urgent requests requiring physical presence at various locations 
throughout the region or state; transport necessary materials, documents, and equipment for 
meetings, presentations, or fieldwork. 
 
Supports the review, update, maintenance of transportation-related impact fees.  
 
Supports the drafting of submittals for grant funding from various local, state, and federal 
funding sources. 
 
And other duties as assigned. 
 
 
Principal Transportation Planner 
In addition to the duties listed above, this position is distinguished by greater scope, 
complexity, independence, and leadership responsibilities, duties may include the following: 
 
Manages and directs the overall operations of the transportation planning section, including 
developing citywide, department and division level policies, principles, procedures, work 
processes and establishes section goals and evaluates achievement against objectives 
 
Leads strategic planning initiatives for transportation and parking programs citywide; 
formulates high-level recommendations for major updates to codes, comprehensive plans, and 
policies with citywide or regional impact. 
 
Directs the review, update, and maintenance of transportation-related impact fees, including 
leading analyses, stakeholder coordination, and recommendations for adjustments. 
 
Identifies and leverages funds to implement planned strategies through drafting and 
coordinating submittals for grant funding from various local, state, and federal funding sources. 
 
Provides high-level representation of the City in regional partnerships, interagency 
collaborations, and policy forums; serves as the primary point of contact for major 
transportation initiatives involving external agencies or stakeholders. 
 
Mentors senior staff and oversees professional development across the section; resolves 
complex operational and personnel issues with minimal supervision. 
 
42 of 409

--- page 43 ---
QUALIFICATIONS 
 
Senior Transportation Planner 
 
Knowledge of: 
 
Transportation, urban planning, and parking principles, practices, standards, trends, 
regulations, metrics, and applicable local, state, and federal laws, codes, and ordinances, 
including those related to zoning and environmental protection. 
 
Research methods and techniques including statistics and statistical analysis. 
 
Techniques used in planning, drafting, and mapping.  
 
Principles and practices of project administration, budgeting, funding, and financing.  
 
Federal, State, and local laws relating to planning and transportation.  
 
Principles and practices of effective supervision, including training and performance 
management and evaluation.  
 
Ability to: 
 
Design and review complex and varied transportation projects, plans, and policies, and 
provide meaningful input and recommendations.  
 
Organize and prioritize multiple varied and competing projects and tasks in an effective 
and timely manner, set priorities, and meet critical deadlines.  
 
Work independently and exercise good judgment. 
 
Communicate clearly and effectively with residents, business owners and community 
groups whether one on one or in group presentations, and both orally and in writing.  
 
Read and understand technical drawings and specifications and perform mathematical 
computations with precision.  
 
Analyze, compile, and evaluate statistical, economic, and technical data, drawing valid 
conclusions and making appropriate recommendations.  
 
Assign, direct, and review the work of subordinates; motivate and evaluate staff. 
 
Direct and oversee consultant activities. 
 
Prepare written reports and make presentations to various groups, commissions, and 
committees. 
43 of 409

--- page 44 ---
Understand relationships between the budget and resources and manage projects within 
available resources.  
 
Utilize computer applications relating to transportation planning. 
 
Work extended or irregular hours. 
 
Principal Transportation Planner 
In addition to the qualifications for the Senior Transportation Planner: 
 
Knowledge of: 
 
Principles and procedures of technical specification writing, plan preparation, and 
construction/project cost estimating.  
 
Capital and operational budget development processes. 
 
Ability to: 
 
Develop community engagement and outreach strategies for projects, planning efforts, 
and programs. 
 
Comply with financial and administrative controls and standards.  
 
Experience and Training Guidelines 
Any combination of experience and training that would provide the required knowledge and 
abilities is qualifying. A typical way to obtain the required knowledge and abilities would be: 
 
Senior Transportation Planner: 
 
Experience: 
At least two years of professional planning experience comparable to that of an 
Associate Transportation Planner, Associate Planner or Associate Engineer equivalent 
experience  
 
Training: 
Equivalent to a Bachelor’s degree from an accredited college or university with major 
coursework in civil engineering, transportation engineering, transportation planning, 
planning or a closely related field. Master’s degree in a closely related field is preferred.  
 
Licenses & Certificate: 
Possession of a valid California Driver’s License. 
 
Certification by the American Institute of Certified Planners is preferred. 
44 of 409

--- page 45 ---
Principal Transportation Planner: 
 
Experience: 
At least two years of professional planning experience comparable to that of a Senior 
Transportation Planner, Senior Planner or Senior Engineer equivalent experience. 
 
Supervisory experience of staff, programs and/or administrative activities is desirable. 
 
Training: 
Equivalent to a Bachelor’s degree from an accredited college or university with major 
coursework in civil engineering, transportation engineering, transportation planning, 
planning or a closely related field. Master’s degree in a closely related field is preferred.  
 
Licenses & Certificate: 
Possession of a valid California Class C Driver’s License. 
 
Certification by the American Institute of Certified Planners is preferred. 
 
ADA SPECIAL REQUIREMENTS: 
Essential duties require the following physical abilities and work environment: 
 
Ability to work in a standard office environment with some exposure to the outdoors.

QUALIFICATIONS
Senior Transportation Planner
Knowledge of:
Transportation, urban planning, and parking principles, practices, standards, trends, 
regulations, metrics, and applicable local, state, and federal laws, codes, and ordinances, 
including those related to zoning and environmental protection.
and applicable laws.
Research methods and techniques including statistics and statistical analysis.
The physical, social, economic, and behavioral factors and constraints involved in 
designing multimodal transportation facilities. 
Modern principles and methods for managing all transportation project phases including 
contract administration. 
Best practices and emerging trends in transportation planning including performance-
based planning, complete streets, multimodal planning, integrated land use and 
transportation planning, and mobility as a service. 
Green infrastructure design elements and their integration with transportation design. 
Symbols, language, and tTechniques used in planning, drafting, and mapping. 
Principles and practices of project administration, budgeting, funding, and financing. 
Principles of citizen outreach and engagement, and techniques for effectively dealing 
with the public and City staff in person, by phone, and via internet/social media to 
provide a high level of customer service. 
Federal, State, and local laws relating to planning and transportation. Provisions of the 
Brown Act. 
English usage, grammar, spelling, vocabulary, and punctuation.
Principles and techniques of managing parking facility operations.
Transportation and urban planning and design principles, practices, trends, regulations, 
standards, measurement, and laws applicable to the area of specialization, with particular 
expertise in multi-modal transportation.

January 12, 2026 
SUBJECT:
Sewer Flush Truck Replacement and Stormwater Combination Truck Procurement — Agreements
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve an alternative purchasing procedure and approve purchase contracts with U-Rock Utility 
Equipment LLC, for the purchase of one (1) new Sewer Equipment Co. of America Model 800-HPR ECO Series IV Flush Truck 
in an amount not to exceed $379,037.46 and one (1) new Sewer Equipment Co. of America (SECA) SECA 900 ECO 6 YD 
Combination Truck in an amount not to exceed $640,075.14; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $25,000.00; 
and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreements in substantially the form presented and issue change 
orders within the contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
The Public Works Field Maintenance Division is responsible for the maintenance and repair of 250 miles of City sewer and 
130 miles of storm infrastructure. Routine sewer and storm system maintenance and repair are essential to ensuring a safe 
and healthy environment for residents and visitors, along with the surrounding natural environment. A key tool for 
maintaining the sewer infrastructure is the use of a flush truck which injects high pressure water into the system to clear 
obstructions and remove debris. For the storm infrastructure, an essential asset is a combination truck, which uses high 
pressure water to clear obstructions but also has a specialized vacuum system to remove debris. By utilizing these 
specialty equipment trucks, City crews ensure that stormwater can flow freely while preventing debris and contaminants 
from entering and polluting the Bay.
The Public Works Field Maintenance Division has requested replacement of unit T57, a 2008 Ford F650 sewer pipe 
cleaning truck which has exceeded its useful life. Staff researched several manufacturers of sewer-cleaning equipment and 
coordinated demonstrations of selected models, which were attended by a delegation from the City Field Maintenance 
and Fleet staff. Through this process, staff identified Sewer Equipment Co. of America (SECA) Model 800-HPR ECO Series IV 
Flush truck (flush truck) as a preferred replacement for unit T57. The flush truck received high marks for low investment 
cost (compared to similar models), safety, and vehicle agility, as well as the ease of use and maintenance of the flush truck 
equipment. Sufficient funding is available in the Vehicle Equipment Replacement Fund for this purchase. 
The Field Maintenance Division is also requesting the addition of one Stormwater Infrastructure Maintenance Truck to 
support the maintenance and repair of the City’s stormwater infrastructure. In recent years, the City has experienced an 
increase in both the intensity and frequency of storm events. In response, the City has expanded its dedicated Stormwater 
team to better meet operational demands.  Staff researched several manufacturers of sewer-cleaning equipment and 
coordinated demonstrations of selected models, which were attended by a delegation from the City‘s stormwater team as 
well as Fleet Department staff. Through this process staff identified Sewer Equipment Co. of America (SECA) SECA 900 ECO 
6 YD Combination Truck (combination truck) as a preferred addition to the fleet. The combination truck received high 
marks for low investment cost (compared to similar models), safety, vehicle agility as well as the ease of use and 
61 of 409

--- page 62 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
maintenance of the Flush Truck and vacuum systems. Funding for this procurement has been allocated within the City’s 
Storm Fund budget.
In alignment with City Council direction and the City’s Green Fleet Initiative, staff evaluated electric vehicle (EV) options as
part of the procurement process, aiming to transition from internal combustion engines to EVs or alternative fuel vehicles
where feasible. As there is no current EV equivalent available for either the flush truck or combination truck, diesel 
internal combustion powered vehicles have been selected that the City will operate on renewable diesel. Renewable diesel 
is an alternative fuel that burns cleaner than conventional petroleum diesel and helps to aid in the reduction of fossil fuel 
dependence. Additionally, the California Air Resources Board (CARB) Zero Emissions Fleet Program requires the offset of 
each new internal combustion-powered truck with one electric powertrain truck. The Public Works Field Maintenance 
Division has met CARB criteria for these purchases with the recent deployment of unit L79, a 2025 Ford Lightning electric 
truck and the Global EV Street Sweeper approved by Council on November 18, 2024, and expected to be delivered in 
Spring 2026.
Staff utilized Sourcewell pricing for the purchases of the flush truck and combination truck. San Mateo Municipal Code 
Section 3.60.070(h)(3) authorizes the City Council to approve an alternative purchasing procedure when it finds doing so is 
in the best interest of the City. Sourcewell is a government organization that solicits, receives, and reviews competitive 
bids for various specialty equipment, including the flush truck and combination truck. Sourcewell has conducted 
competitive public bids to select vehicle vendors to achieve competitive pricing and has selected U-Rock Utility Equipment 
LLC and awarded Sourcewell Contract #101221-SCA. The City may rely on bids obtained from Sourcewell because it has 
solicited, received, and reviewed competitive bids for the desired flush truck and combination truck through its 
cooperative purchasing program. Through this pricing structure, the City realizes cost savings off manufacturer’s suggested 
retail price. Based on the above, staff recommends the purchase of this SECA Model 800-HPR ECO Series IV Flush Truck 
and SECA 900 ECO 6 YD Combination Truck from U-Rock Utility Equipment LLC and establishing a contingency reserve of 
$25,000 to allow for price fluctuations from market instability.
BUDGET IMPACT:
Sufficient funding is available in the Vehicle and Equipment Replacement Fund for the flush truck purchase and within the 
Storm Fund for the combination truck purchase.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
These purchases are not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that they will not cause a physical 
change in the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

Att 3 – Combination Truck Agreement

APPROVING AN ALTERNATIVE PURCHASING PROCEDURE TO APPROVE PURCHASE CONTRACTS WITH U-ROCK

$640,075.14
WHEREAS, the Public Works Field Maintenance Division oversees the maintenance and repair of the 
City’s sewer and storm drainage infrastructure; and
WHEREAS, the maintenance and repair of the City’s sewer and storm drainage infrastructure is essential 
to maintaining a safe and healthy environment for both residents and visitors; and
WHEREAS, a primary tool in maintaining the sewer infrastructure is the use of a specialized flush truck 
and for the storm drainage infrastructure a specialized combination truck; and  
WHEREAS, the City Council is being asked to award a purchase contract for one (1) new Sewer 
Equipment Co. of America (SECA) Model 800-HPR ECO Series IV Flush Truck to U-Rock Utility Equipment LLC, to 
replace an existing unit which has exceeded useful life.; and 
WHEREAS, the City Council is being asked to award a purchase contract for one (1) new Sewer 
Equipment Co. of America (SECA) SECA 900 ECO 6 YD Combination Truck to U-Rock Utility Equipment LLC; and 
WHEREAS, as part of the transition to a Green Fleet, staff continually research electrical options during 
the procurement process and aim to replace vehicles with battery electric or alternative-fueled vehicles when 
available; and
WHEREAS, when there is no current electric vehicle equivalent available, a diesel internal combustion 
powered vehicle operating on renewable diesel is the preferred alternative fuel option; and
WHEREAS, the purchase of the Sewer Equipment Co. of America (SECA) Model 800-HPR ECO Series IV 
Flush Truck aligns with the City’s Green Fleet Initiative as the unit will be operated on renewable diesel, an 
alternative fuel; and
WHEREAS, the purchase of the Sewer Equipment Co. of America (SECA) SECA 900 ECO 6 YD Combination 
Truck aligns with the City’s Green Fleet Initiative as the unit will be operated on renewable diesel, an alternative 
fuel; and
WHEREAS, the City has met the requirements of the California Air Resources Board Regulations which 
allow for the purchase of one (1) new Sewer Equipment Co. of America (SECA) Model 800-HPR ECO Series IV 
Flush Truck and one (1) new Sewer Equipment Co. of America (SECA) SECA 900 ECO 6 YD Combination Truck; 
and
WHEREAS, staff recommends utilizing Sourcewell’s pricing through U-Rock Utility Equipment LLC, for the 
purchase of this Sewer Equipment Co. of America (SECA) Model 800-HPR ECO Series IV Flush Truck and SECA 900 
ECO 6 YD Combination Truck; and
WHEREAS, San Mateo Municipal Code Section 3.60.070(h)(3) authorizes the City Council to approve an 
alternative purchasing procedure when it finds doing so is in the best interest of the City; and

IV Flush Truck and one (1) New Sewer Equipment Co. of America (SECA) SECA 900 ECO 6 YD 
Combination Truck from U-Rock Utility Equipment LLC is not a project subject to CEQA, because 
it can be seen with certainty that there is no possibility that the purchase of a sewer flush truck 
or combination truck to support the maintenance of City’s sewer and storm drainage 
infrastructure may have a significant effect on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 
15061(b)(3).)

Equipment Co. of America (SECA) Model 800-HPR ECO Series IV Flush Truck and SECA 900 ECO 6

the City’s best interest for these reasons:
a.

bids for various specialty equipment; and
b.
The Sewer Equipment Co. of America (SECA) Model 800-HPR ECO Series IV Flush Truck 
and SECA 900 ECO 6 YD Combination Truck are the Public Works Field Maintenance 
Division’s desired vehicles; and

Combination Truck and U-Rock Utility Equipment LLC, was selected pursuant to 
Sourcewell Contract #101221-SCA; and
d.
The City may rely on Sourcewell’s selected vendor and contract, as it offers competitive 
pricing without the need for the City to conduct its own bidding process.

The purchases of one (1) new Sewer Equipment Co. of America (SECA) Model 800-HPR ECO 
Series IV Flush Truck in the amount of $379,037.46 and one (1) new Sewer Equipment Co. of 
America (SECA) SECA 900 ECO 6 YD Combination Truck in the amount of $640,075.14 and 
establishment of a contingency reserve in the amount of $25,000.00 are approved.

form presented and issue change orders within the contingency amount.

SECTION 18 - MEDIATION

"blindfolded" process.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

PURCHASE CONTRACT 
FOR ONE (1) NEW SEWER EQUIPMENT CO. OF AMERICA (SECA) SECA 900 ECO 6 YD COMBINATION 
TRUCK FROM U-ROCK UTILITY EQUIPMENT LLC
This Purchase Contract (“Contract”), made and entered into this day of ___________________, 
by and between the CITY OF SAN MATEO, a municipal corporation existing under the laws of the State 
of California (“CITY”), and U-ROCK UTILITY EQUIPMENT LLC, a CORPORATION (“VENDOR”).
RECITALS:
A.
CITY desires to purchase certain ONE (1) NEW SEWER EQUIPMENT CO. OF AMERICA 
(SECA) SECA 900 ECO 6 YD COMBINATION TRUCK hereinafter described.
B.
CITY desires to engage VENDOR to provide these ONE (1) SEWER EQUIPMENT CO. OF 
AMERICA (SECA) SECA 900 ECO 6 YD COMBINATION TRUCK by reason of its qualifications and 
experience and VENDOR has offered to provide the required goods on the terms and in the manner set 
forth herein.
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS AGREED as follows:
SECTION 1 - PURCHASE
The goods to be purchased from VENDOR under this Contract are described in Exhibit A to this 
Agreement, which is attached and incorporated by reference.
SECTION 2 - PRICE AND TAXES
All prices shall be as stated in this Contract and are firm and not subject to escalation.  
This purchase is subject to all California sales tax.  Municipalities are exempt from federal excise and 
transportation taxes.  Prices shall exclude these taxes.  
SECTION 3 - PAYMENT
Unless otherwise agreed in writing, payment terms shall be net thirty (30) days from date of 
receipt of invoice or acceptance of goods, whichever occurs last.  Invoices must cite the purchase order 
number to prevent delay in payment.  All invoices must be mailed to City of San Mateo, Attn:  Accounts 
Payable, 330 West 20th Avenue, San Mateo, CA 94403.

SECTION 4 - DELIVERY AND PERFORMANCE
Time is of the essence in the performance of this Contract.  If delivery of goods cannot be made 
at the specified time, VENDOR shall promptly notify the CITY of the earliest possible date for delivery.  
Notwithstanding such notice, if VENDOR for any reason fails to deliver goods within the time specified 
or to the CITY’s satisfaction the CITY may terminate this Contract or any part thereof without liability 
except for goods previously provided and accepted.  The CITY’s receipt or acceptance of all or part of a 
non-conforming delivery shall not constitute a waiver of any claim, right or remedy the CITY has under 
this Contract or applicable law. 
SECTION 5 - SHIPMENT AND INSPECTION
VENDOR assumes full responsibility for all transportation, transportation scheduling, packing, 
handling, insurance, and other services associated with delivery of all products.  No charges for 
transportation containers, packing, etc., will be allowed the vendor unless so specified in this Contract.  
All shipments shall be F.O. B. City of San Mateo Corporation Yard, 1961 Pacific Blvd, San Mateo CA 
94403.  Transportation charges shall be shown as a separate item on the invoice.
The CITY may revise shipping instructions as to any goods not as yet shipped.  The CITY shall 
have the right to inspect any or all of the goods at VENDOR’s place of business or upon receipt by the 
CITY.  By reason of its failure to inspect the goods, the CITY shall not be deemed to have accepted any 
defective goods or goods which do not conform to the specifications provided or to have waived any of 
the CITY’s rights or remedies arising by virtue of such defects or non-conformance.  VENDOR shall be 
responsible for payment of shipping for the return of any defective goods.  Shipping documents and 
invoices must cite the Purchase Order number.
SECTION 6 - WARRANTIES
In addition to any other expressed or implied warranties and unless otherwise agreed in 
writing, VENDOR warrants that all products delivered hereunder will be new, suitable for use as 
described, of the grade and quality specified, free from all defects in design, material and 
workmanship; in conformity with all samples, drawings, descriptions and specifications furnished; in 
compliance with all applicable federal, state and local laws and regulations, and free of any liens and 
encumbrances.  These warranties shall not be deemed to exclude VENDOR’s standard warranties or 
other rights or warranties which the CITY may have or obtain.

SECTION 7 - INDEMNITY
VENDOR agrees to hold harmless and indemnify CITY, its elected and appointed officials, 
employees, and agents from and against any and all claims, loss, liability, damage, and expense arising 
out of VENDOR’s performance of this Contract, except for those claims arising out of CITY’s sole 
negligence or willful misconduct.  VENDOR agrees to defend CITY, its elected and appointed officials, 
employees, and agents against any such claims. The VENDOR’S duty to indemnify shall survive 
expiration or early termination of this Agreement. 
SECTION 8 - TERMINATION
This Contract may be terminated by mutual consent of both parties or by the CITY at its 
discretion.  The CITY may cancel an order for goods at any time with written notice to VENDOR, stating 
the extent and effective date of termination.  Upon receipt of this written notice, VENDOR shall stop 
performance under this Contract as directed by the CITY.  If the Contract is terminated, VENDOR shall 
be paid in accordance with the terms of the Contract for goods delivered and accepted.
SECTION 9 - REMEDIES
In the event of VENDOR’s breach of this Contract, City may take any or all of the following 
actions, without prejudice to any other rights or remedies available to the City by law:  (a) require 
Vendor to repair or replace such goods, and upon VENDOR’s failure or refusal to do so, repair or 
replace the same at VENDOR’s expense; (b) reject any shipment or delivery containing defective or 
nonconforming goods and return for credit or replacement at VENDOR’s option, said return to be 
made at VENDOR’s cost and risk; (c) cancel any outstanding deliveries and treat such breach by 
VENDOR as VENDOR’s repudiation of this contract.  In the event of the CITY’s breach hereunder, 
VENDOR’s exclusive remedy shall be VENDOR’s recovery of the goods or the purchase price payable for 
goods shipped prior to such breach.
SECTION 10 - COMPLIANCE WITH LAW
VENDOR warrants that it will comply with all federal, state, and local laws, ordinances, rules 
and regulations applicable to its performance under this Contract.  VENDOR shall obtain and maintain 
throughout the life of the Contract all permits or licenses required in connection with the manufacture, 
sale, and shipment of the products ordered under this Contract.  
SECTION 11 - ASSIGNMENT
VENDOR shall not delegate or subcontract any duties and services or assign any rights or claims 
under this Contract without the CITY’s prior written consent.

SECTION 16 - COSTS AND ATTORNEY FEES
Attorney fees in total amount not exceeding $5000, shall be recoverable as costs (by the filing 
of a cost bill) by the prevailing party in any action or actions to enforce the provisions of this 
Agreement.  The above $5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court, 
appellate court, or otherwise, and regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions.  It 
is the intent of this provision that neither party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for 
attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to enforce the provisions of this Agreement.

prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

January 12, 2026 
SUBJECT:
Local Roadway Safety Plan — Grant Acceptance, Appropriation, Budget Transfer, and Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to accept a Transportation Improvement Program Grant Award in the amount of $959,000, authorize 
an appropriation of $295,400 of the grant funding, and approve a budget transfer of $38,273 of the City’s Measure S funds 
from the Quick Build Mobility Program project account to the Local Roadway Safety Plan – Priority Package 1 project 
account in the Capital Project Fund; approve an agreement with CSW/ST2 for design engineering services in the amount of 
$247,574 for the Local Roadway Safety Plan - Priority Package 1 project; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of 
$50,000 for the agreement; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form 
presented and issue amendments within the approved contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
The City adopted its Local Roadway Safety Plan (LRSP) in May 2024 to establish a framework and process for identifying, 
analyzing, and prioritizing roadway safety improvements throughout the City. The LRSP is a community-driven and data-
informed plan aimed at improving roadway safety performance. It provides a framework that prioritizes traffic safety 
improvements on city streets based on crash patterns, trends, and crash risk analysis. The City aspires toward zero 
fatalities and severe injuries by employing a Safe System approach, focusing on safe vehicles, speeds, road users, road 
design, and post-crash care. The LRSP was developed in collaboration with engineering, enforcement, education, equity, 
and emergency service strategies. The LRSP analyzed traffic safety performance, crash patterns, and recommended 
strategic and proven solutions to improve safety at priority locations. It includes focus areas and identifies high-priority 
locations based on crash history, stakeholder collaboration, and community feedback. 
Following City Council direction from the May 2024 City Council meeting to prioritize implementation of the top 10 
locations in the LRSP, staff pursued funding for those sites lacking allocated resources. Staff identified priority locations 1, 
2, 4, and 6 as the highest-priority unfunded sites and developed LRSP - Priority Package 1 (Project), which includes the 
following intersections:
•
El Camino Real & 22nd Avenue 
•
El Camino Real & 27th Avenue 
•
Humboldt Street & Tilton Avenue 
•
Humboldt Street & Indian Avenue 
•
Humboldt Street & Santa Inez Avenue
•
Hillsdale Boulevard & Franklin Parkway/Highway 101 Ramps 
•
Hillsdale Boulevard & Norfolk Street
Pursuit of Funding
On December 9, 2024, City Council adopted a Resolution of Local Support (City Resolution No. 114 (2024)) authorizing the 
89 of 409

--- page 90 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
filing of an application for funding assigned to the Metropolitan Transportation Commission (MTC), committing any 
necessary matching funds, and stating assurance to complete the project. 
In May 2025, the City was notified by MTC that it had been awarded $959,000 in federal grant funding through the 
Transportation Improvement Program (TIP) (MTC Resolution No. 4202, Revised). The funds are provided through the 
Surface Transportation Block Grant (STP), which requires an 11.47% local match totaling $124,248. These funds are 
programmed for preliminary engineering, construction, and construction engineering. On October 17, 2025, the TIP was 
officially amended to include funding for the project.
Proposal Results
A Request for Proposals (RFP) for the project was posted to the City bid/proposal page on October 15, 2025. A total of two 
(2) proposals were received prior to the close of the submittal period ending at 4:00 PM, November 5, 2025. Staff 
reviewed and scored the proposals based on the following criteria: quality and completeness; quality and effectiveness of 
the solution; experience and qualifications; proposer’s prior record with City or other municipalities; and the proposer’s 
ability to perform the work within the specified duration. Reviewers used the rubric described in the RFP to score the 
proposals. Per federal contracting requirements, proposal evaluations cannot consider price in the selection process. A 
summary of the proposal scoring results from the four reviewers is presented in the table below:
RANK
CONSULTANT
AVG TOTAL SCORE
1
CSW/ST2
71.50
2
SANDIS
69.00
Consultant interviews were conducted on November 17, 2025, to gather additional information and clarification on the 
consultants‘ experience and key staff. Based on a review of the proposals and interviews, staff selected CSW/ST2 as the 
preferred consultant. CSW/ST2’s extensive experience directly managing projects utilizing federal funding through the 
Caltrans Local Assistance Program was a key factor in differentiating their team from the other consultant and justifying 
their selection for this project.
Staff and the consultant team have identified some project tasks that Caltrans has a low likelihood of requiring as part of 
their approval process. Staff are requesting a contingency reserve of $50,000 to allow flexibility to quickly activate these 
tasks, should Caltrans determine they are required, to keep the project on schedule and complete all work (through 
construction) within the grant timeline.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The City was awarded funds on April 9, 2025, by MTC through a resolution revising the One Bay Area Grant (OBAG2) 
Program to program additional funds for Housing Incentive Pool (HIP) projects. The City has been awarded federal funds 
from the Surface Transportation Block Grant (STP) Program to complete all phases (design, environmental, and 
construction) of the LRSP Priority Package 1 (Project). 
The City will accept $295,400 in HIP funding for Fiscal Year 2025-26 towards Preliminary Engineering and Design with a 
required local match of $38,273. For Fiscal Year 2026-27, the project will receive the remaining grant allocation $663,600 
for Construction with a required local match of $85,977. The remaining grant funding and required match for Fiscal Year 
2026-27 will be requested for appropriation through the annual budget development process of the Capital Improvement 
Program. 
To meet the local match obligations for the Preliminary Engineering phase of the grant, staff has identified $38,273 of 
available Measure S funding from the Quick Build Mobility Program (Project No. 46R026) to be transferred to the Local 
Roadway Safety Plan – Priority Package 1 (46R033) project account.
With the acceptance and appropriation of the HIP grant funds to the Local Roadway Safety Plan – Priority Package 1 
Project, there will be sufficient funds available to award this agreement to CSW/ST2 for design engineering services and 
90 of 409

--- page 91 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
establish the requested contingency reserve.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This Project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation, repair, 
maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities, 
mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or former use. (CEQA 
Guidelines Section 15301.)

SECTION 15 - WAIVERS 
 
The waiver by either party of any breach or violation of any term, covenant, or condition of this 
Agreement or of any provisions of any ordinance or law shall not be deemed to be a waiver of such 
term, covenant, condition, ordinance or law or of any subsequent breach or violation of the same or of 
any other term, condition, ordinance, or law. The subsequent acceptance by either party of any fee or 
other money which may become due hereunder shall not be deemed to be a waiver of any preceding 
breach or violation by the other party of any term, covenant, or condition of this Agreement or of any 
applicable law or ordinance. 
 
SECTION 16 – SEVERABILITY 
 
 
If any term or portion of this Agreement is held to be invalid, illegal, or otherwise 
unenforceable by a court of competent jurisdiction, the remaining provisions of this Agreement shall 
continue in full force and effect. 
 
SECTION 17 - COSTS AND ATTORNEY FEES 
 
 
Attorney fees in total amount not exceeding $5000, shall be recoverable as costs (by the filing 
of a cost bill) by the prevailing party in any action or actions to enforce the provisions of this 
Agreement.  The above $5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court, 
appellate court, or otherwise, and regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions.  It 
is the intent of this Agreement that neither party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for 
attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to enforce the provisions of this Agreement. 
 
SECTION 18 - NON-DISCRIMINATION 
 
 
CONSULTANT warrants that it is an Equal Opportunity Employer and shall comply with 
applicable regulations governing equal employment opportunity.  Neither CONSULTANT nor any of its 
sub-consultants shall discriminate in the employment of any person because of race, color, national 
origin, ancestry, physical handicap, medical condition, marital status, sex, or age, unless based upon a 
bona fide occupational qualification pursuant to the California Fair Employment and Housing Act.
