SECTION 19 - MEDIATION 
 
 
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to 
mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be 
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one 
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw. 
 
 
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties. 
 
SECTION 20 - LITIGATION 
 
 
CONSULTANT shall testify at CITY's request if litigation is brought against CITY in connection 
with CONSULTANT's services under this Agreement.  Unless the action is brought by CONSULTANT, or 
is based upon CONSULTANT's wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate CONSULTANT for preparation for 
testimony, testimony, and travel at CONSULTANT's standard hourly rates at the time of actual 
testimony.

Scope of Work 
From our experience in developing active transportation projects, we have developed the following 
work plan. 
TASK 1: OPPORTUNITIES & CONSTRAINTS 
In this initial phase, our team will collaborate with staf, community members, and stakeholders to 
understand the opportunities and constraints guiding the safety improvements. To facilitate 
concept development and support future funding initiatives, our team will engage stakeholders in 
establishing project-related goals. 
1.1 Project Kickoff. Key members of our team will host a meeting with City staff to introduce the 
project team and to review and discuss key project elements. We will present and facilitate a 
discussion on the following: 
A. Project Goals. Beginning with the City’s goal to develop a planning document for the 
corridor, we will collaborate with the City to draft project-speciﬁc goals for the University 
Avenue community engagement and visioning process, as well as goals for the design and 
implementation of the Grand Corridor vision. These goals will need to align with those of 
the City of East Palo Alto’s Vista 2035 General Plan, where “University Avenue will be 
transformed from a cut-through corridor into a beautiful mixed-use boulevard with high-
density housing, neighborhood-serving businesses, and offices that capitalize on the City’s 
proximity to Silicon Valley. 
B. Funding Opportunities. It is essential to plan the project consistently with upcoming 
funding opportunities. We want to learn about the City’s past success with grants and any 
thoughts on upcoming opportunities. 
C. Community Engagement. Our team will share a draft Community Engagement Strategy. 
The City’s feedback, including experience and project-speciﬁc engagement goals, will be 
discussed and incorporated into the ﬁnal strategy. 
1.2 Community Engagement Plan. We will prepare a concise, milestone-based outreach plan 
aligned with the federal grant schedule. The plan will identify key audiences (residents, 
103 of 409

--- page 104 ---
businesses, schools, transit agencies, neighborhood and homeowner associations, advocacy 
groups) active within a ¼ mile of each of the priority intersections; incorporate CEQA/NEPA 
notiﬁcation requirements and include Title VI, Environmental Justice, Limited English 
Proﬁciency (LEP), and ADA compliance measures. Following each outreach activity, we will 
provide a Stakeholder Feedback Summary Report summarizing participant input, responses, 
and design implications. A comprehensive Public Involvement Record will be maintained for 
inclusion in the CEQA/NEPA administrative record and Caltrans submittals. 
1.3 Data Collection and Field Review. To support the preliminary design effort and reﬁne the 
extent of technical studies required, our team will complete the following: 
A. Data Collection. The team will collect and review documents associated with the following 
topics: 
• 
LRSP’s crash datasets 
• 
Statewide Integrated Traffic Records System (SWITRS) reports 
• 
Existing traffic, parking, and collision data. 
• 
Existing utility records. 
• 
Property Boundary and easement information from the City and Caltrans. 
B. Field Review. Our team will perform a site walk. 
1.4 Existing Photometric Analysis Memorandum (Existing PAM). Our team will complete a 
photometric analysis of the existing intersections to ensure that the proposed pedestrian and 
vehicular-scale lighting is consistent with City and State standards. This will include ensuring 
lighting levels are both dark-sky and temperature-friendly, and will consist of recommendations 
for lighting and ﬁxture upgrades. Analysis will be performed at El Camino Real & 22nd Ave, 
Hillsdale Blvd & Franklin Pkwy and Hillsdale Blvd & Norfolk Street only. 
1.5 Existing Conditions Mapping. Our team will compile existing condition mapping for each 
of the Humboldt Avenue intersection (Indian Ave, Santa Inez Ave, Tilton Ave), including the 
following. Any existing conditions mapping at El Camino Real & 22nd Ave and El Camino 
Real & 27th Ave, Hillsdale Blvd & Franklin Pkwy and Hillsdale Blvd & Norfolk Street will be 
an optional service. 
A. Property Boundary. Our team will locate and resolve the right-of-way along each of the 
Humboldt Avenue intersection (Indian Ave, Santa Inez Ave, Tilton Ave). 
B. Monument Preservation. We will locate and preserve record monuments in accordance 
with the Business & Professions Code §8771; Streets & Highways §732 & §732.5, §1492.5, 
§1810.5; and Penal Code §605. We will locate these monuments and develop special 
provisions requiring the contractor to ﬁle a pre-construction corner record with San Mateo 
County, showing three (3) reference control points tied to each monument. 
C. Survey. Our team will collect topography, using a combination of conventional topographic 
ﬁeld survey and aerial drone methods, which generally will include face of building, 
sidewalk, face of curb, street centerline, pavement grade breaks, and surface utilities. 
104 of 409

--- page 105 ---
D. Utilities. Our team will collect utility records as well as measure the depth of gravity 
systems and water valves to establish horizontal and vertical data. 
E. Utility Potholing (OPTIONAL SERVICE). If the as-built data is inconclusive, we will 
complete potholing of utilities at up to 10 locations across the seven (7) intersections. Our 
contractor will backﬁll the potholes with a controlled low-strength material. 
F. Prepare Base Map. CSWST2 will develop a detailed base map integrating topography, 
boundary, and utility information, as well as provide a high-resolution orthorectiﬁed aerial 
photograph. 
1.6 Community Outreach. We will initiate community outreach and build project awareness by 
establishing online communications and distributing print materials, as outlined in the 
Community Engagement Plan. Efforts at this stage will include the following activities. 
A. Project Website. Our team will establish a project website that provides the project 
purpose and schedule, education on relevant technical concepts, and design concepts as 
developed. This site will offer an opportunity for visitors to offer project feedback. We will 
use this as a tool to provide responses to community concerns. 
B. Project Communications. Outreach will focus on communities surrounding the six priority 
intersections. We will employ: multilingual notiﬁcations (English, Spanish, Chinese) via 
email to existing City mailing list(s), direct mail to all owners and occupants within a ¼ of 
the intersection, and print ﬂyers posted at bus stops and community gathering places. We 
will engage neighborhood and homeowner associations to expand the reach of project 
communications. In addition, we will provide the City with project narratives and project 
area maps for utilization in the City’s social media and other communication channels. 
C. Engagement. We will attend/facilitate one Pop-up event or virtual community meeting and 
attend standing meetings for up to four community organizations/associations. 
1.7 Contract Management. CSWST2 will be responsible for the overall management of our design 
team, including the following: 
A. Project Management. CSWST2 will manage the design team as well as track progress, 
schedule, and budget. We will be responsible for documenting all design decisions and 
keeping an official record of the project. Furthermore, we will submit monthly progress 
reports that identify completed tasks, budget status, and issue status. 
B. Quality Control/ Quality Assurance. An independent team member will review our 
documents prior to submittal to the City. 
C. Grant Management. CSWST2’s Grant Manager will manage document compliance with the 
approved grant requirements. 
D. Meetings. The team will attend bi-weekly project management meetings with City Staff, key 
stakeholders, and the project team. 
Deliverables. We will provide electronic (PDF and native format) of the following documents: 
• 
Kick-off Meeting Agenda and Meeting Summary 
105 of 409

--- page 106 ---
• 
Draft and Final Community Engagement Plan 
• 
Communication Materials 
• 
Existing Conditions Mapping 
• 
Existing Photometric Analysis 
TASK 2: CONCEPTUAL DESIGN 
Using the data collected in Task 1 and guided by the concepts and collision data from the LRSP, we 
will evaluate the trafic safety measures and prepare a conceptual plan for City approval. 
2.1 Conceptual Options. CSWST2 will evaluate options, considering traffic operations along with 
other factors such as bicycle and pedestrian access, transit access, safety, and connectivity. A 
key goal will be to balance vehicle, bicycle, pedestrian, and transit access through each 
intersection. We will prepare at least two options for each intersection. 
A. We will evaluate each of the options in conformance with the project goals, including 
quantifying the following conditions. 
• 
Improve safety for all users. 
• 
Consistency with the policies established in the LSRP. 
• 
Improve bicycle and pedestrian access and connectivity. 
B. To summarize our ﬁndings, we will prepare a memorandum regarding the feasibility of the 
safety improvements, which includes the following for each option: 
• 
Narrative description of the proposed design. 
• 
Plan and section graphics. 
• 
An assessment of the options’ conformance to the project’s goals. 
• 
Estimate of implementation cost. 
2.2 Community Outreach and Engagement. We will conduct outreach to community members 
and key stakeholders within the focus area around each of the six priority intersections to share 
conceptual options, key evaluative criteria, and education on technical concepts. We will 
gather feedback to identify key areas of concern and support. We will employ: 
• 
Multilingual notiﬁcations (English, Spanish, Chinese) via email, direct mail, and ﬂyers; 
• 
Digital engagement tools such as online surveys; 
• 
One Pop-up event or virtual community meeting and attendance at standing meetings 
for up to four community organizations/associations. 
Following each outreach activity, we will provide a Feedback Summary Report summarizing 
participant input, responses, and design implications. The project website will be updated to 
include feedback themes. 
2.3 Contract Management. We will complete the tasks as identiﬁed in Task 1.7, including 
attending up to two (2) coordination meetings. 
106 of 409

--- page 107 ---
Deliverables. We will provide electronic (PDF and native format) of the following documents: 
• 
Draft and ﬁnal Options as well as feasibility study. 
• 
Webpage and Online Survey updates. 
• 
Communication materials, Engagement materials, and Feedback summaries. 
• 
General Meetings agendas, presentation, and minutes. 
TASK 3: PRELIMINARY ENGINEERING 
With approval of the preferred option, our team will prepare the design to the 35% level, allowing for 
reﬁnement of costs. This submittal will include narratives, fees, and exhibits that can serve as the 
basis for future grant applications as well as the basis for environmental review under CEQA and 
possibly NEPA. 
3.1 Preliminary Design (35%). We will develop a preliminary plan establishing the geometry of the 
roadway serving pedestrians, bicyclists, and motorists. This will include the following 
elements: 
A. Streetscape Plans. To document the design, we will prepare the following plans, including: 
• 
Title and Key Map Sheets 
• 
Roadway Layout Plans Illustrating sidewalks, medians, buffers, and curb ramps. 
• 
Striping and Signage Plans 
• 
Typical Cross Sections 
• 
Traffic signal modiﬁcation plan 
• 
Street lighting plan 
B. Right of Way. We will research the existing right of way and will provide a veriﬁcation 
memorandum illustrating that no right of way acquisition is required for the project’s 
construction. 
C. Cost Estimate. We will reﬁne the cost model developed in Task 2.1. 
3.2 Community Outreach and Engagement. We will conduct outreach to community members 
and key stakeholders within the focus area around each of the six priority intersections to share 
the draft Preliminary Design, identify the role of previous engagement in guiding design 
development, key evaluative criteria, and education on technical concepts. We will gather 
feedback to identify key areas of concern and opportunity for reﬁnement. We will employ: 
2 - Multilingual notiﬁcations (English, Spanish, Chinese) via email, direct mail, and ﬂyers; 
3 - Digital engagement tools, such as online surveys; 
4 - One Pop-up event or virtual community meeting and attendance at standing meetings for up 
to four community organizations/associations.

--- page 108 ---
Following each outreach activity, we will provide a Feedback Summary Report summarizing 
participant input, responses, and design implications. The project website will be updated to 
include feedback themes. 
3.2 Contract Management. We will complete the tasks as identiﬁed in Task 1.7, including 
attending up to three (3) coordination meetings. 
Deliverables. We will provide electronic (PDF and native format) of the following documents: 
• 
Webpage and Online Survey updates.

Documents for the 35% PS&E.

Right of Way Memorandum 
TASK 4: LOCAL ASSISTANCE COORDINATION 
With approval of the preliminary engineering, our team will coordinate with Local Assistance to 
secure environmental and right-of-way clearance to allow the project’s bidding. 
4.1 CEQA Assessment. We will compile a Categorical Exemption that includes the following 
elements. 
A. Project Description. We will prepare the project description and present the project 
summary information as identiﬁed on the Environmental Checklist Form in Appendix G of 
the CEQA Guidelines. The project description will include a discussion of the key 
characteristics of the project site and vicinity, project objectives, details of the proposed 
project, the planning and approval process, and the anticipated project schedule. 
B. CEQA Categorical Exemption. Section 21084 of the Public Resources Code (PRC) provides 
guidelines for projects that have been determined not to have a signiﬁcant effect on the 
environment and are therefore determined to be exempt from the provisions of CEQA. The 
proposed project is likely to fall into the ﬁrst category (Class I) of categorically exempt 
projects, as described in Section 15301, Existing Facilities. We will document the 
determination for the exempt status in a Notice of Exemption (NOE) accompanied by a 
supporting memorandum. 
4.2 NEPA Assessment. Our team will coordinate with Local Assistance to provide a Categorical 
Exclusion as an activity listed in 23 CFR 771.117(c), item 22; projects that would take place 
entirely within the existing operational right-of-way, including features associated with the 
physical footprint of the transportation facility. Since the walls are a replacement for an existing 
structure, we assume they would fall into exclusion. To support these ﬁndings, our team will 
complete the following studies: 
A. NEPA Project Description. We will support the City in preparing the Preliminary 
Environmental Study (Exhibit 6-A), Field Review (Exhibit 7-B), and Roadway Data Forms 
108 of 409

--- page 109 ---
(Exhibit 7-C) based upon the 10% submittal. We will support the City during the ﬁeld review 
and incorporate Local Assistance’s conditions into the construction documents to satisfy 
the NEPA categorical exclusion. 
B. Biological Resources (OPTIONAL SERVICE). As these projects are located within the built 
environment, we believe the completion of a Natural Environmental Study is not required, 
and standard mitigations are acceptable. However, we have allocated a fee for a biologist 
to complete a data search and ﬁeld reconnaissance of up to three locations, as well as the 
Zone 7 channel. 
C. Visual Assessment. This will address the visual impact of tree removal. 
D. Contamination. We will complete an assessment of contamination within the project area 
using the Geotracker website. This will include a narrative implementing standard 
mitigations. 
E. Standard Memoranda. We will provide standard memoranda with reference to traffic 
control, water quality, and construction staging. 
4.3 Public Utilities. Our team will coordinate with public utilities, including PGE, Comcast, AT&T, 
and City utilities, to ensure their infrastructure is integrated into the design and consistent with 
the Utility Certiﬁcation requirements of Local Assistance. This will include the following items. 
A. Preliminary Notice. Our team will prepare a formal notiﬁcation, also known as A Letters, to 
the utilities within 10 days of notice to proceed. This will include a coordination meeting at 
the City’s office (or online) to discuss the project and schedule. 
B. Detailed Coordination. As we advance the design, our team will submit plans at the 35% 
and 100% levels of completion, also known as the B and C Letters/ Plans. This will include 
a coordination meeting and a summary of the next steps in the process. 
C. New Utility Services. Revisions to traffic signals and new pedestrian-scale lighting may 
require new utility services. Our team will complete applications and the necessary 
supporting documents for these services. 
4.4 Local Assistance. We will support staff in assembling documents for Local Assistance, 
including: 
A. Right of Way Certiﬁcation. CSWST2 will complete Local Assistance Form 13-B “Right of 
Way Certiﬁcation” for the project, documenting that the City has permanent rights-of-way 
as well as utility clearances to construct the project. We assume this will be Certiﬁcation 
Number 1 of 2. Additionally, while the contractor may need to enter private property to 
complete the work, it is for the beneﬁt of the private property owner, which can be 
completed through a standard right of entry process. We will prepare up to ten (10) right of 
entry documents. 
B. Request for Authorization. With the completion of the 100% documents and 
encroachment permit, we will submit the following: 
• 
Request for Authorization Form

--- page 110 ---
• 
PS&E Certiﬁcation and Checklist 
• 
Field Review From 
• 
Finance Letter 3-O 
• 
DBE Form 
• 
ROW Certiﬁcation 
• 
Plans and Speciﬁcations 
4.5 Contract Management. We will complete the tasks as identiﬁed in Task 1.7, including 
attending up to four (4) coordination meetings. 
Deliverables. We will provide electronic (PDF and native format) of the following documents: 
• 
CEQA Project Description and Categorical Exemption.

Meeting agendas, presentation, and minutes. 
TASK 5: FINAL ENGINEERING 
With approval of the preliminary design, our team will develop ﬁnal construction documents for 
bidding in response to conditions found during the environmental phase and within the available 
budget. 
5.1 Streetscape Plans, Speciﬁcations, and Estimate. Our team will prepare documents to the 
90% levels of completion. This will include the following: 
A. Streetscape Plans. To document the design, we will prepare the following plans in 
accordance with the Caltrans Plan Preparation Manual: 
• 
Title, Key Map, and General Sheets

Demolition Plan

Lighting Plan

Traffic Signal Plan 
• 
Erosion Control Plans 
B. Technical Studies. Our team will develop the following technical studies: 
110 of 409

--- page 111 ---
• 
Photometric Analysis Memorandum (PAM). Our team will complete a ﬁnal 
photometric analysis to ensure the proposed vehicular and pedestrian scale lighting is 
consistent with City and State standards. This will include ensuring lighting levels are 
both dark-sky and temperature-friendly. 
• 
Stormwater Control Plan. We will evaluate requirements for green infrastructure 
based on proposed improvements. Our team will develop the required features 
consistent with San Mateo County’s C.3 standards. We will complete the MRP C.3 
Checklist and, if required, prepare a draft Stormwater Control Plan in accordance with 
the Construction General Permit order 2009-0009-DWG. 
• 
Hydrology and Hydraulics Report. We will provide a Hydrology and Hydraulics Report 
indicating there is no expected change with the surface drainage patterns or the 
hydraulic capacity of the existing storm drain system. 
C. Speciﬁcations. Our team will develop Technical Speciﬁcations in the City standard format 
for the project, consistent with Federal requirements. We will integrate the City’s front-end 
speciﬁcations into the contract documents and develop Special Provisions to the 2018 
Caltrans Standard Speciﬁcations and City Division IX – Traffic Control Devices and Division 
X – Electrical Work. 
D. Cost Estimate/ Bid Schedule. We will update our cost model consistent with the design 
and funding program. 
E. Comments. Our team will document all comments received from the City and others in a 
matrix and provide a response to each. 
F. Outreach. Our team will continue to build on the outreach strategy developed in Task 1, 
providing multilingual notiﬁcations via website updates, email, and direct mail to maintain 
community awareness of project status. In addition, we will support staff in seeking Council 
approval to bid the 100% documents. 
5.2 Permitting. Our team will assist the City in preparing and submitting the Caltrans 
Encroachment Permit. 
5.3 Final Plans, Speciﬁcations, and Estimate. With receipt of the E76, the team will prepare the 
documents developed in Tasks 5.1 for bidding. 
5.4 Contract Management. We will complete the tasks as identiﬁed in Task 1.7.

TASK 6: BIDDING AND CONSTRUCTION SUPPORT 
6.1 Bidding Support. Our team will assist during the bidding phase by assisting in outreach, 
attending the pre-bid meeting, responding to contractor requests for information, preparing 
bid addenda as necessary, and reviewing bids submitted. 
6.2 Construction Support. The team will attend a pre-construction meeting. During 
construction, the team will review shop drawing submittals, respond to contractor 
questions, provide technical guidance, visit the site on ﬁve (5) occasions during 
construction, review ﬁve (5) change order requests, and prepare a punch list near the 
completion of construction. After construction, we will prepare record drawings based on 
the contractor’s markups. The City of San Mateo will review contractor submittals. 
Deliverables. We will provide electronic (PDF and native format) of the following documents: 
• 
Bid addenda. 
• 
Conform plan and speciﬁcations for use in construction. 
• 
Digital ﬁles 
• 
Response to request for information.

EXHIBIT C 
 
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS 
 
 
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE  
Coverage shall be at least as broad as: 
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit 
applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the 
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit. 
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if CONSULTANT 
has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no less than 
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage. 
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury 
or disease.  
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate 
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and shall 
be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT. 
Other Insurance Provisions 
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions: 
Additional Insured Status 
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used). 
Primary Coverage 
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it. 
Notice of Cancellation 
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City. If a Notice 
of Cancellation endorsement is not available, CONSULTANT shall ensure the requisite Notice of 
115 of 409

--- page 116 ---
Design Professional Services 2024 
 
Page 12 of 12 
Rev 1/24 
Cancellation is specified in the Certificate of Insurance.  In the event the Notice of Cancellation is not 
specified in the Certificate of Insurance, Consultant shall be responsible for providing the City the 
requisite notice as specified in this Exhibit C.  
Waiver of Subrogation 
CONSULTANT hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
CONSULTANT may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  
CONSULTANT agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of 
subrogation endorsement from the insurer.   
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions 
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the CONSULTANT to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof 
of ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within 
the retention.   
Acceptability of Insurers 
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City. 
Verification of Coverage 
CONSULTANT shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies 
of the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the CONSULTANT’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

City Council

Alex Khojikian, City Manager

Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
January 12, 2026 
SUBJECT:
Citywide Facilities Condition Assessment Project — Budget Appropriation
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to authorize a supplemental budget appropriation in the amount of $25,000 from the unassigned 
General Fund balance in the Capital Project Fund to the Citywide Facilities Condition Assessment Project in order to 
address additional work. 
BACKGROUND:
The City's property portfolio includes over a hundred buildings of varying types, ages, and conditions. To optimize resource 
use, the Public Works Department Facilities Division created a Citywide maintenance program and assessed each facility 
individually, identified potential issues based on their physical condition, and prioritized repairs according to the severity 
of deficiencies using a weighted scoring system. 
The Facilities Condition Assessment (FCA) evaluated and documented the physical condition of the City's buildings, which 
included their structures and systems. This was achieved through a review of existing documentation, consultations with 
City staff, and on-site inspections of each property. A comprehensive report was produced, detailing the probable cost to 
address any significant physical or design deficiencies identified during the assessment. 
In addition to the core building evaluations, the assessment also identified areas requiring more specialized investigation 
that extended the overall scope of work. These included Hazardous Materials Sampling to determine the presence of 
asbestos, lead-based paint, or other regulated substances, as well as more in-depth studies of structural roof components 
at specific facilities where initial observations suggested potential concerns. Based on input from the City’s current on-call 
professional services consultants who provided preliminary cost ranges using recent project data, typical sampling 
protocols, and anticipated labor and testing requirements, staff estimates $25,000 is needed to complete these 
supplemental investigations. This figure reflects the consultants’ professional judgment regarding the effort, materials, and 
analysis needed to thoroughly evaluate conditions not fully captured through visual inspection alone. These supplemental 
tasks will provide a deeper understanding of potential risks and remediation needs, ensuring that all areas of concern are 
comprehensively assessed and appropriately addressed.
Public Works is requesting a total appropriation of $25,000 to cover the costs of the supplemental work. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Approval of the proposed resolution will authorize an appropriation of $25,000 from the General Fund's unassigned fund 
balance in the Capital Project Fund to the project, in order to fund the additional assessment work necessary for the 
Citywide Facilities Condition Assessment Project (46F030).

RESOLUTION NO. ____ (2026)
AUTHORIZING AN APPROPRIATION IN THE AMOUNT OF $25,000 FROM THE CITY’S UNASSIGNED GENERAL

PROJECT TO ADDRESS ADDITIONAL SUPPLEMENTAL WORK 
WHEREAS, the City’s portfolio consists of wide range of facilities of various types, ages, and conditions 
requiring maintenance to optimize resource use; and 
WHEREAS, the Public Works Department initiated a Citywide Facilities Condition Assessment (FCA) to 
evaluate and document the physical condition of City buildings and their structural and system components; and
WHEREAS, the FCA conducted through a review of existing documentation, consultations with City staff, 
and on-site inspections of each facility, resulting in a comprehensive report identifying deficiencies and 
associated probable repair costs; and
WHEREAS, the FCA identified areas requiring more specialized investigation that extended the overall 
scope of work including Hazardous Materials Sampling and in-depth studies of structural roof components; and 
WHEREAS, the Public Works Department has determined that an additional estimated $25,000 is 
required to complete supplemental work; and

Fund is available to appropriate the $25,000 to satisfy the additional funding needs.

involve any commitment to any specific project which may result in a potentially significant physical 
impact on the environment.  (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).) 
2.
An appropriation of $25,000 from the General Fund unassigned fund balance in the Capital Project 
Fund to the Citywide Facilities Condition Assessment Project (46F030) budget is authorized.

SUBJECT:
Clean Water Program Labor Compliance Consultant – Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 2 to the agreement with TSG Enterprises, Inc. DBA The Solis Group for on-call labor compliance 
services for the Clean Water Program in an amount not to exceed $50,000, for a total amount of $450,000; and authorize 
the Public Works Director to execute the amendment in substantially the form presented. 
BACKGROUND:
The City of San Mateo Clean Water Program (CWP) is a comprehensive program to upgrade the aging wastewater 
collection system and the Wastewater Treatment Plant (WWTP) to provide reliable services for years to come. The success 
of the CWP depends on the completion of several complex construction projects funded by a variety of sources. 
State and Federal labor regulations apply to each project based on the scope and funding. To ensure compliance with all 
applicable laws, the City Council approved an agreement with TSG Enterprises, Inc. DBA The Solis Group, on May 6, 2019, 
to perform the labor compliance monitoring and reporting for the CWP. 
The initial on-call agreement amount was established to provide labor compliance support on the earlier WIFIA-funded 
construction projects such as WWTP GMP-1, Underground Flow Equalization System, Dale Ave Pump Station 
Improvements, and Lift Stations Improvement construction packages. Amendment No. 1 was approved on June 7, 2021, 
for additional support on the remaining WIFIA-funded components of the CWP, including WWTP GMP-2 and GMP-3, 
Pacific Boulevard Force Main, Delaware Street Sewer Relief, El Camino/Flores Relief Sewers, and El Camino/28th 
Avenue/Colegrove Relief Sewers. 
Construction of the WWTP GMP-3 is approximately 97% complete and in its final stages and construction of the new 
treatment process facilities is complete. Process seeding, startup, and performance testing is expected to occur in the 
November 2025 – January 2026 timeframe with the new WWTP anticipated to be in full service by January 2026. The 
remaining scope of work on the existing WWTP and final completion of miscellaneous sitewide improvements is 
anticipated to be complete by June 2026. 
As a result of the GMP-3 construction contract extension, extension of associated labor compliance services is also 
necessary. Staff estimates an additional $50,000 should be added to TSG’s on-call agreement to support the monitoring 
and reporting through final completion of the WWTP GMP-3. The current term of TSG’s on-call agreement is through June 
30, 2026. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Sufficient funds are available in the WWTP and Flow Management Upgrade and Expansion Project (46t003) to fund 
120 of 409

--- page 121 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Amendment No. 2 to TSG’s on-call agreement for labor compliance services for the CWP. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
The City prepared a Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR) in accordance with the California 
Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) (SCH No. 2015032006). The PEIR was certified by City Council on June 6, 2016. In 
accordance with CEQA, the Final PEIR serves as the primary environmental compliance document for implementation of 
the Clean Water Program. The City prepared an Addendum to the Final PEIR that were approved on July 16, 2018 
(Addendum 1) and April 15, 2019 (Addendum 2). This work is within the scope of the project evaluated in the PEIR and 
Addenda.

EXHIBIT A2  
SCOPE OF SERVICES 
The Consultant is to provide Federal, State, and local labor monitoring services for 
contracts funded by grants, loans, enterprise funds, or other funds; projects may include 
construction of various types of public wastewater system infrastructure. The WWTP 
Upgrade and Expansion Project is partially funded with CWSRF State funding and 
EPA/WIFIA Federal Funding. Tasks to be performed will include, but not be limited to 
the following:  
1. Establish and maintain payroll files in conformance with standards established by the 
City of San Mateo CWP and grantor agencies.  
2. Perform forms collection, review and verifications; certified payroll review; 
apprenticeship program compliance oversight; on-site monitoring; field reviews and all 
related follow-ups including assistance with electronic submissions of certified payroll 
and all related documents into the California Department of Industrial Relations (DIR).  
3. Address labor compliance inquiries from contractors.  
4. Provide technical guidance to contractors, as needed, to aid in contractor electronic 
registration process as well as completion and submission of electronic payroll forms. 
5. Monitor receipt of “one-time” documents required by federal grant agencies, e.g. 
certificate of employee authorization and statement of fringe benefits and Apprentice 
programs.  
6. Review, monitor and report weekly payrolls submitted by contractors and 
subcontractors.  
7. Provide the CWP with a concise monthly report, mentioning specific work and tasks 
performed by the firm.  
8. Follow-up and report on delinquent payrolls and wage underpayment in accordance 
with grant agency and CWP requirements.  
9. Interview one employee per trade per month and verify interview results against 
submitted payrolls.  
10. Respond to audit requests for information received from the State of California 
Department of Industrial Relations (DIR), the Federal Department of Labor (DOL) and 
other regulatory authorities.  
11. Provide DBE and other Disadvantaged Business Enterprise Programs verification 
reports upon the request of the City, if needed.

Agenda Number:  12
Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR

PREPARED BY:
Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
January 12, 2026 
SUBJECT:
Polymer Injection System Project Design and Engineering Services During Construction — Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to authorize an appropriation in the amount of $1,200,000 from the Sewer Fund reserves to the 
Wastewater Treatment Plant Polymer Injection Project in the Capital Projects Fund; approve an alternative purchasing 
procedure to enter into an agreement with Kennedy/Jenks Consultants, Inc. to provide professional services for design and 
engineering services during construction in an amount not to exceed $311,055; establish a contingency amount of 
$60,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute this agreement and task amendments within the contingency 
amount in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
Sludge Cake Pumps No. 1 and No. 2 were installed in 2020 as part of the Immediate Action Projects Package 2 (IAP2) 
project at the Wastewater Treatment Plant (WWTP). This agreement will authorize design of a polymer injection system to 
add polymer into the sludge cake pump discharge piping with the goal of reducing cake pump operating pressures. Sludge 
cake is the end product of the solids digestion process in the treatment of wastewater. It is a non-free-flowing material 
typically containing 18 – 25% dry solids. In an effort to reduce cake pump operating pressures and resultant wear and tear 
on the cake pumping systems, this project will design a system to inject polymer to lubricate the cake pump piping, 
thereby reducing resistance and resultant system pressure as the sludge cake is pumped to the storage hoppers prior to 
off-haul and disposal. 
Kennedy/Jenks Consultants, Inc. was selected using an alternative purchasing procedure since the firm was previously 
involved in the design of the cake pump discharge piping system and has proposed completing the design, bidding, and 
engineering services during construction for an amount not to exceed $311,055, which staff finds reasonable. Pursuant to 
San Mateo Municipal Code Section 3.60.070(h)(3), approving an agreement with Kennedy/Jenks Consultants, Inc. 
(Kennedy Jenks) is in the best interests of the City because Kennedy Jenks was previously involved in the design of the cake 
pump system for the IAP2 project, and its familiarity with the system is essential to completing a successful project within 
a reasonable time frame and with reasonable costs. Staff is also requesting an appropriation of $1,200,000 to cover still-to-
be-determined project and construction costs that will be addressed through separate procurement processes.
  
BUDGET IMPACT:
There are sufficient funds in the Sewer Fund reserves for this appropriation to the Capital Projects Fund in the amount of 
$1,200,000 for the Wastewater Treatment Plant Polymer Injection Project (46T191). 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:

Scope of Work 
Task 1: Project Management and QA/QC - Design and Bid Phase 
This task consists of project monitoring and administration and project quality assurance/quality 
control (QA/QC) activities. 
Task 1.1 – Project Initiation and Coordination 
KJ will set up the project within KJ’s accounting system and initiate the Project with KJ’s design 
team, outlining the scope and budget, and develop a baseline schedule. KJ will implement 
management procedures and actions to facilitate delivery of services and products. KJ will 
provide management and oversight for in-house project personnel including review and 
monitoring of project budget and progress.  
Task 1.2 – Monthly Reports and Invoicing 
KJ will prepare and submit monthly invoices electronically to the City. Monthly project progress 
status reports will be prepared and delivered the City to support monthly invoices.   
Deliverables: 
•
Monthly Status Reports and Invoices (Electronic Adobe PDF)
Task 1.3 – Meetings 
KJ will attend the following meetings during the design phase. All meetings are assumed to be 
virtual. 
•
KJ will attend a project kick-off meeting with the City to introduce the project team,
discuss the project scope, specific project procedures, and schedule. This meeting is
assumed to be up to 1 hours in duration and attended by up to 4 KJ staff.
•
KJ will attend monthly progress meetings to review technical issues with the internal KJ
team. These meetings are assumed to be up to 1 hour in duration and occur every four
weeks over a design span of 4 months, attended by up to 2 KJ staff.
•
The City is expected to provide a single, consolidated list of comments to the 90%
Design to KJ two weeks prior to the 90% design workshop. KJ will attend one (1)
workshop with the City to review comments for the 90% design submittal. The workshop
is assumed to have a 2-hour duration and will be attended by up to 4 KJ staff.
Deliverables: 
•
Kick-off meeting agenda and notes (electronic)
•
Monthly progress meeting notes (electronic)
•
90% design workshop meeting notes (electronic)

Task 2: Design Phase 
Task 2.1: 90% Design Documents and OPCC 
KJ will incorporate responses to comments on the final IAP2 Polymer Injection System design 
documents (as submitted on February 13, 2025). KJ will prepare additional drawings and 
specifications for a standalone bid package developed to a 90% level of completion and a 
related Opinion of Probable Cost (OPCC). A list of anticipated drawings is included at the end of 
this Scope of Work. The OPCC will be an Association for the Advancement of Cost Engineering 
(AACE) International Class 3 estimate and will be projected to the midpoint of the construction 
period. The documents prepared will compose the 90% Design submittal package and 
submitted to the City for review. 
It is assumed that KJ will redline the City’s Construction Agreement, Notice Inviting Sealed 
Proposals, Accepted Proposal, Special Provisions, Faithful Performance Bond, and Labor and 
Material Bond. The City will incorporate KJ’s redlines and comments and provide the updated 
documents to KJ for review. If additional edits are needed, KJ will coordinate with the City for 
incorporation. KJ will prepare Division 01 specifications using the Division 01 specifications from 
the IAP2 Project as a starting point. If the City identifies other relevant Division 01 specifications 
for inclusion, they will be provided to KJ for editing. KJ will assemble the Construction 
Agreement, Notice Inviting Sealed Proposals, Accepted Proposal, Special Provisions, Faithful 
Performance Bond, Labor and Material Bond, and Division 01 into the 90% Design submittal 
package. 
Deliverables: 
•
90% Design Drawings, Specifications, and OPCC (electronic)
Task 2.2: Final Design Documents and OPCC 
The City shall provide a single, consolidated list of comments to the 90% Design for KJ at least 
two weeks prior to the 90% design submittal workshop for KJ to review and provide responses. 
KJ will then incorporate agreed-upon modifications to the Final Design Documents and prepare

possible. These documents will be provided to KJ within a week of the notice to proceed.
No additional Division 01 sections are currently anticipated, only edits to the IAP2
sections.
•
The design will be based on the previously identified Netzsch polymer feed pumps and
polymer injection ring for coordination and consistency with existing equipment.

No survey, geotechnical, or utility investigations will be conducted.
•
No permitting assistance is included.

design clarification are assumed to remain valid, with no technical changes anticipated.
•
The existing discharge piping can accommodate the polymer ring and the existing pipe
support provides sufficient space to install the polymer ring.
•
The existing pump room at ground floor has sufficient space for polymer system
equipment and components including totes and pumps. The existing structure at grade
is assumed to have sufficient capacity to support any new equipment, pumps, and pipe
supports as confirmed during development of IAP2 DC 12. Any verification of existing
structures are excluded. The estimate does not include time for retrofit of existing
foundations. It is assumed that all new construction anticipated will be within the limits of
the prescriptive compliance method found in the existing California Building Code.
•
Pipe supports and anchorage will be designed by Contractor as part of a deferred
submittal.
•
Electrical equipment support pads are excluded from the scope; it is assumed the
polymer pump control panel will be anchored directly into the existing concrete.
•
The anchorage for new equipment (i.e. polymer pumps, control panel) will be designed
by the Contractor as part of a deferred submittal.
•
The existing design documents package is complete with technical content for the
polymer injection system. Effort assumes updates to reflect a standalone bid package
and no further engineering is required.
•
Programming of programmable logic controller (PLC) and instrumentation is excluded.
•
Relocation of existing utilities is excluded.

samples, operations and maintenance manuals, and product data required to be submitted by 
the Contractor. Review will be for substantial conformity with the intent of the Contract drawings 
and specifications. Such review will be only for conformance with the design concepts and 
general compliance with the project’s Contract Documents. It will not include review of 
quantities, dimensions, weights or gauges, fabrication processes, construction methods, 
coordination with the work of other trades, or construction safety precautions, all of which are 
the sole responsibility of the Contractor. It is assumed that up to 27 submittals (including 
resubmittals), each requiring on average 5 hours, will be reviewed by KJ. 
Deliverables: 
•
Reviewed submittals with indicated disposition (electronic)
Task 5.2: RFIs 
KJ will provide responses to the Contractor’s Requests for Information (RFIs). RFIs will be 
furnished to KJ by the City, and written responses will be provided to the City for dissemination 
within an average of seven (7) working days of receipt of an RFI. It is assumed that up to 25 
RFIs, each requiring on average 4 hours, will be reviewed by KJ. 
In addition to Contractor RFIs, it is assumed that the City’s Construction Manager will have 
informal requests for information that go beyond what is expected from administering the 
construction contract. To account for these requests, KJ assumes that up to 15 informal RFIs, 
each requiring on average 4 hours, will be reviewed by KJ. 
142 of 409

--- page 143 ---
Scope of Work 
Page 6 
Deliverables: 
•
RFI responses (electronic)
Task 5.3: Site Observations 
KJ will make up to two visits to the construction site involving 2 individuals for an average 
duration of 4 hours on-site, to review the progress and quality of the construction work. The 
visits will observe the general quality of the work at the time of the visit. For each site visit, KJ 
will prepare a site observation report documenting the areas observed and comments regarding 
general conformance with the design requirements. KJ will review items of concern with the 
Construction Manager before leaving the site. 
Deliverables: 
•
Site Observation Reports (electronic)
Task 5.4: Construction Progress Meetings 
KJ will attend regularly organized construction coordination/progress meetings organized by the 
Construction Manager for the City. KJ’s attendance is assumed to be virtual. A total of 16 
meetings (bi-weekly meetings for 7 months), assumed to be up to 1 hour in duration will be 
attended by up to 2 KJ staff. Meeting agenda and minutes will be prepared by the Construction 
Manager for the City and reviewed by KJ. 
Deliverables: 
•
Comments to the City’s meeting agenda and minutes, if any (electronic)
Task 5.5: Change Order Reviews 
KJ will support the City, as requested, with evaluation of change orders or potential change 
orders. As requested, KJ will review notices and correspondence issued by the Contractor and 
provide a written opinion of the validity of Contractor request. It is assumed that the City’s 
construction management staff will have primary responsibility for evaluation of and responses 
to Contractor-issues notices and correspondence. This task provides as-needed support for one 
change order or potential change order review, requiring up to 32 hours. 
Deliverables: 
•
Written responses for change order-related issues (electronic)
Task 5.6: Record Drawings 
KJ will prepare Record Drawings for the Project using the drawing markups of construction 
changes provided by the Contractor. For estimating purposes, it is assumed that 22 drawings 
will be updated, each requiring on average 8 hours.

Deliverables: 
•
Record Drawings (electronic)
Task 5.7: Startup 
KJ will participate in startup activities for the polymer injection system. This will be limited to 
review and comment of submitted startup procedures, in-person attendance to a 6-hour startup 
activity, and preparation of field notes. In-person startup is assumed to be attended by up to 2 
KJ staff. 
Deliverables: 
•
Startup Field Notes (electronic)

costs identified in the Proposal Fee Estimate. Additional effort will only be provided as
authorized through a contract modification.
•
Construction management services are by others.

EXHIBIT C 
 
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS 
 
 
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE  
Coverage shall be at least as broad as: 
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit 
applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the 
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit. 
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if CONSULTANT 
has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no less than 
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage. 
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury 
or disease.  
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate 
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and shall 
be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT. 
Other Insurance Provisions 
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions: 
Additional Insured Status 
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used). 
Primary Coverage 
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it. 
Notice of Cancellation 
152 of 409

--- page 153 ---
Design Professional Services 2024 
Page 10 of 10 
Rev 1/24 
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City. If a Notice 
of Cancellation endorsement is not available, CONSULTANT shall ensure the requisite Notice of 
Cancellation is specified in the Certificate of Insurance.  In the event the Notice of Cancellation is not 
specified in the Certificate of Insurance, Consultant shall be responsible for providing the City the 
requisite notice as specified in this Exhibit C.  
Waiver of Subrogation 
CONSULTANT hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
CONSULTANT may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance. 
CONSULTANT agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of 
subrogation endorsement from the insurer.   
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions 
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the CONSULTANT to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof 
of ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within 
the retention.   
Acceptability of Insurers 
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City. 
Verification of Coverage 
CONSULTANT shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies 
of the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the CONSULTANT’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Agenda Report
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
Agenda Number:  13
Section Name: PUBLIC HEARING
Account Number: 
File ID: 25-10764
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Alex Khojikian, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Community Development Department
MEETING DATE:
January 12, 2026 
SUBJECT:
2033 La Salle Drive - Zoning Reclassification, Zoning Code Amendment, and Planning Application for an Early Childhood 
Education Center — Ordinance Introduction
RECOMMENDATION:
Introduce an Ordinance to approve a Zoning Reclassification from R1-B to R1-B/Q8, and a Zoning Code Amendment to 
provide development standards for an educational facility and find it exempt from CEQA pursuant to Section 15061(b)(3) 
(Common Sense Exemption); and adopt a Resolution to approve the Planning Application (Special Use Permit, Site Plan and 
Architectural Review and Site Development Planning Application) for the development of an Early Childhood Education 
Center subject to the findings for approval and conditions of approval, and find it exempt from CEQA pursuant to Section 
15303 (New Small Structures Exemption).
BACKGROUND:
The Carey School is a private educational institution serving students from pre-kindergarten through fifth grade since 1955.
Their main elementary school campus is located at 1 Carey School Lane off of La Salle Drive, and their preschool program is 
located at 3900 Alameda de las Pulgas within the Transfiguration Church. The Carey School is seeking approval to construct 
an Early Childhood Education Center at 2033 La Salle Drive to relocate the preschool operation to be next to its main campus. 
To support this request, the proposal includes a zoning code amendment and a zoning reclassification from R1-B (One Family 
Dwellings) to R1-B/Q8 (One Family Dwellings /Qualified Overlay District 8). 
The Planning Commission held a public hearing to consider the request on December 9, 2025, and, following public 
comments and deliberation, voted unanimously to recommend that the City Council approve the project with an added 
recommendation that the City investigate establishing a no-parking zone on the La Salle cul-de-sac. Staff has evaluated this 
recommendation, and provided additional information in the parking section of this report. 
Pursuant to SMMC 27.06.060, and because the planning application includes multiple reviews requiring action at different 
levels, the City Council will consider and act upon the entire application. The Draft Ordinance for the zoning reclassification 
and zoning map amendment is included as Attachment 1, and the Draft Resolution for the Special Use Permit (SUP), Site 
Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR) and Site Development Planning Application (SDPA) is included as Attachment 2.
 
SITE DESCRIPTION:
The 0.6-acre site (26,380 square feet) consists of a single parcel currently developed with an 1,851-square-foot single-family 
residence and a 640-square-foot attached accessory dwelling unit. The site is accessed via the La Salle Cul-de-sac and a 
private creek runs along the southern boundary of the property. Surrounding uses include single-family residential 
development to the north, Junipero Serra High School to the east, the existing Carey School campus to the south, and multi-
family apartment buildings to the west across La Salle Drive. The site has a General Plan land use designation of Residential 
Very Low and is zoned R1-B (One Family Dwellings). A location map showing the site and its vicinity is included as 
154 of 409

--- page 155 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Attachment 3.
 
PROJECT DESCRIPTION:
The applicant proposes to demolish all existing structures, and redevelop the site with a new Early Childhood Education 
Center (“Project”) consisting of a one-story, 5,908 square-foot building and associated site improvements. The building 
includes six classrooms designed to accommodate up to 75 preschool-aged children (ages 2–5 years) and 16 teachers. The 
Project also includes a trash enclosure, an outdoor play area located on the south side of the site, and a teaching garden on 
the north side. The Project provides eleven on-site parking spaces and proposes the use of an off-site parking facility at 
1900–2000 Alameda de las Pulgas to meet the remaining required parking spaces. A cover letter from the applicant with 
additional information about the proposed use is included as Attachment 4, and the Project plans are included as Attachment 
5.
 
APPLICABLE CODE AND POLICY REVIEW:
General Plan and Zoning Code
The General Plan land use designation for the Project site is Residential Very Low. The proposed Project provides a 
neighborhood-serving childcare use within a residential district, which is supported by Land Use Policy 3.5 and Public Services 
and Facilities Policy 6.5.  A list of applicable General Plan policies and a discussion of the Project’s conformance to them is 
included in the Draft Resolution in Attachment 2. 
 
Zoning Reclassification and Zoning Code Amendment
The applicant is requesting a zoning reclassification from R1-B to R1-B/Q8 and an amendment to the Q8 Overlay to establish 
development standards for the Early Childhood Education Center. The City has previously applied Qualified Overlay 
designations to private educational facilities to address their operational needs, including St. Matthew’s Catholic Parish and 
School (Q7) and Junipero Serra High School (Q6). These overlays provide alternative floor area, parking, and development 
standards tailored to the educational use of these properties. Extending the Q8 Overlay to include the Project site will allow 
the Project to meet the off-site parking facility requirement. While the base R1-B zoning requires parking to be located on 
the same parcel or within 200 feet of the site, the existing Q8 Overlay allows off-site parking within a 1,000-foot radius. The 
Project’s proposed off-site parking facility at 1900–2000 Alameda de las Pulgas is located within this 1,000-foot radius.
The requested amendments to the Q8 Overlay includes allowing uncovered parking within the front and side setbacks and 
increasing rear yard projections for building awnings. The Project is proposing uncovered off-street parking within the front 
setback. Pursuant to SMMC Section 27.18.110(c), required parking spaces may not be located within the front or side yard 
setback in One-Family Dwelling districts; therefore, an amendment to the Q8 Overlay is required to permit this configuration. 
In addition, the R1-B district currently allows awnings up to eight feet in height within the rear yard setback. The proposed 
amendment to the Q8 Overlay would allow awnings up to nine feet in height within the rear yard setback. The proposed 
zoning code amendments are included in the Ordinance (Attachment 1), and the amendment language shown in track 
changes is provided in Attachment 6.
Extending and amending the Q8 Overlay for the Early Childhood Education Center maintains consistency with prior Q 
overlays for private institutions. The proposed zoning reclassification and code amendments would facilitate 
implementation of General Plan policies, while ensuring that development standards remain compatible with the 
surrounding residential neighborhood and that regulatory oversight is maintained. With the adoption of the proposed 
overlay, the Project will conform to all applicable zoning code standards.  A Factual Data Sheet listing the applicable zoning 
standards and the Project’s conformance to them is included as Attachment 7.
Special Use Permit (SUP)
The applicant proposes to establish an Early Childhood Education Center within the One Family Dwellings (R1-B) zoning 
district. Pursuant to SMMC Section 27.18.30, private educational facilities are allowed in the R1 zoning district with approval 
of a SUP. The Q8 overlay zone also requires that all uses within the overlay obtain a SUP. Other private educational 
institutions located within the R1-B zoning district with a Q overlay include St. Matthew’s Catholic Parish and School (Q7) 
and Junipero Serra High School (Q6).  The SUP includes conditions of approval that regulate enrollment, hours of operation, 
and on-site activities.  An SUP is also required for the demolition of the existing single-family residence and off-site parking 
155 of 409

--- page 156 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
facility. A detailed discussion on the off-site parking facility is provided in the parking section. Findings and conditions to 
support approval of the SUP are included in the Draft Resolution (Attachment 2).
Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR)
The Project requires SPAR approval pursuant to Municipal Code Section 27.08.030 for the construction of a new private 
educational facility. The proposed development includes a one-story, 5,908 square-foot building with associated site 
improvements. The facility incorporates six classrooms, a teaching garden, and a play area located on the south side of the 
building to minimize noise impacts on residences to the north, and eleven off-street parking spaces in the front yard area. 
Vehicular access would be provided via a one-way circular driveway from La Salle Drive, with one loading berth located along 
the street frontage. Landscaping and site improvements include the installation of 29 new trees along the site perimeter. A 
private creek runs along the southern edge of the property; however, the Project maintains appropriate setbacks from the 
creek to avoid impacts. The Project’s Riparian Assessment is included as Attachment 11.
The proposed one-story stucco building is compatible in scale and architectural character with the surrounding residential 
development and the adjacent Carey School campus, and it complies with the R1-B building height and plate height 
requirements. Findings and conditions to support approval of the SPAR are provided in Attachment 2.
Traffic Analysis
Trip Generation 
A Traffic and Parking Evaluation Memorandum for the Project was prepared by Kimley-Horn (Attachment 8). The Carey 
School currently operates a preschool facility at 3900 Alameda de las Pulgas, which is proposed to be relocated to the Project 
site adjacent to the existing elementary school. Based on the observed trip overlap between the two facilities (an average 
of 60% over the last six years), a 50% carpool reduction was applied, reflecting that approximately half of the Early Childhood 
Education Center students have siblings at the elementary school and would carpool. With the carpool reduction, the Project 
is expected to generate a net increase of 133 daily trips, including 28 net new trips during the AM peak hour, 27 net new 
trips during the school PM peak hour (2:30 p.m. to 3:30 p.m.), and 27 net new trips during the PM peak hour.
Vehicle Miles Traveled
The Project is exempt from Vehicle Miles Traveled (VMT) analysis pursuant to California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) 
Guidelines Section 15064.3. The City’s Traffic Impact Analysis Guidelines establish thresholds of significance and identify 
certain land uses that may be screened out of VMT evaluation. Under these guidelines, local-serving retail and public service 
uses of 50,000 square feet or less are presumed to have a less than significant VMT impact. Schools and educational facilities 
are recognized by the City and by many other jurisdictions as local-serving uses based on their operational characteristics. 
Therefore, the Project is screened out of VMT analysis.
Local Transportation Analysis
In accordance with the City’s Local Transportation Impact Analysis Guidelines, a traffic operations study was conducted for 
the nearest intersection at W. 20th Avenue and La Salle Drive. The study evaluated Level of Service (LOS) and vehicle queuing 
to assess potential impacts from the Project. Incorporating a 50% carpool rate, the analysis concluded that the intersection 
would continue to operate at an acceptable LOS C or better during all peak periods. Condition 57 has been included to ensure 
that an average trip overlap with Carey School of at least 50% is maintained into the future as long as the facility is in 
operation. Also, the Project is expected to generate a queue of approximately 2.5 vehicles within the parking lot and increase 
existing La Salle cul-de-sac queues by no more than one vehicle (approximately 25 feet). Therefore, the Project complies 
with the City’s Transportation Impact Analysis Guidelines.
 
Parking and Circulation
The Project requires 23 parking spaces pursuant to SMMC Section 27.64.160. The Project provides 11 on-site parking spaces 
and utilizes an off-site parking facility at 1900–2000 Alameda de las Pulgas to provide an additional 15 spaces. On-site parking 
will be used for parent drop-off and pick-up activities, while the off-site parking facility will serve staff. The parking analysis 
for 1900–2000 Alameda de las Pulgas demonstrates that the site has sufficient surplus parking capacity to lease 15 spaces 
to the Project. With the addition of these off-site spaces, the Project’s total parking supply exceeds Code requirements by 
156 of 409

--- page 157 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
three spaces. Per Condition 65, the school must maintain a shared parking agreement for the use of the off-site spaces for 
the duration of its operation. The parking analysis is provided in Attachment 8.
 
A Parking and Traffic Management Plan was prepared for the Project to ensure safe and efficient circulation (Attachment 
9).  The plan merges drop-off and pick-up operation with the existing Carey School, identifies designated drop-off and pick-
up locations for each age group, staggers start and end times, and establishes a monitoring program to ensure safe and 
efficient circulation.  The school will provide five dedicated staff to monitor and direct traffic during drop-off and pick-up 
periods in accordance with the Parking and Traffic Management Plan. Condition 62 requires that the school distribute an 
updated Parking and Traffic Plan annually to parents, detailing circulation routes and assigned times and location for student 
drop-off and pick-up.  
 
At the Planning Commission meeting, staff was directed to investigate establishing a no-parking zone on the La Salle cul-de-
sac in response to neighborhood concerns about the lack of parking along La Salle Drive. Currently, non-conforming “No 
Parking” signs have been placed along the cul-de-sac without City approval. Public Works evaluated the area and concluded 
that parking can be restricted on the La Salle cul-de-sac during school drop-off and pick-up peak hours to improve traffic 
flow. A memo prepared by Public Works recommends adding a condition of approval requiring the applicant to remove the 
non-conforming signs and install City-standard signs and poles at the designated drop-off and pick-up locations. The memo 
is provided as Attachment 12, and Condition 31 was revised to incorporate this recommendation.

In accordance with Government Code sections 65090 and 65091 and the City’s Municipal Code public noticing requirements, 
the notice for this public hearing was posted in three public facilities and published in the San Mateo Daily Journal 
newspaper, and sent to the following parties at least 10 days in advance of City Council meeting:

added to the Project notification list.
 
PUBLIC COMMENTS:
Prior to the Planning Commission meeting, five community members submitted multiple comments raising concerns related 
to traffic, parking, noise, and potential environmental impacts, as well as a petition opposing the Project with more than 40 
signatures. Staff also received five letters in support of the Project, citing the need for high-quality early childhood facilities 
within the City, along with a petition containing more than 50 signatures.
Staff received clarifying questions from a member of the Planning Commission prior to the meeting and provided responses. 
These responses are included in Attachment 13. During the Planning Commission meeting, eight members of the public 
comments were heard by the Commissioners, and four additional comments were submitted via email. Comments in 
support of the Project emphasized the City’s need for high-quality childcare, positive experiences with The Carey School’s 
educational programs, and observed improvements in traffic flow due to the school’s staggered drop-off and pick-up 
procedures. Comments raising concerns about the Project focused on potential construction noise, traffic impacts on La 
Salle Drive, Alameda de las Pulgas and 20th Avenue, as well as on-street parking conditions along La Salle Drive.
All written public comment are included in Attachment 14. Any additional public comments submitted after agenda 
publication will be posted to this item on the City’s Public Meeting Portal as “Post Packet Public Comments.”
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This Zoning Reclassification and Zoning Map Amendment are exempt from California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) 
Guidelines pursuant to Common Sense Exemption (14 CCR Section 15061(b)(3)).  The Common Sense exemption applies to 
Projects “Where it can be seen with certainty that there is no possibility that the activity in question may have a significant 
effect on the environment, the activity is not subject to CEQA.”  The proposed reclassification to extend the Q8 overlay, 
while retaining the underlying R1-B zoning, has no potential to cause a physical change to the environment.  The amendment 
157 of 409

--- page 158 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
is administrative in nature and does not, by itself, authorize any physical development, demolition, or land disturbance. 
Future physical improvements or changes in use on the site would remain subject to separate discretionary approvals, 
including a SUP and SPAR, as required under Municipal Code Section 27.60.180(h) (Qualified Overlay District 8).
The development of the Project itself is categorically exempt from the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) pursuant 
to CEQA Guidelines Section 15303, New Construction or Conversion of Small Structures (Class 3). The Project is consistent 
with the example provided under Section 15303(c), which includes “a store, motel, office, restaurant, or similar structure in 
urbanized areas.” The exemption also applies to up to four such commercial buildings not exceeding 10,000 square feet in 
floor area on sites zoned for such use, provided the Project does not involve the use of significant amounts of hazardous 
substances, that all necessary public services and facilities are available, and that the surrounding area is not environmentally 
sensitive.
 
Specifically, the proposed Project meets the criteria for this exemption as it:

Is located within an urbanized area;

Has a total floor area of less than 10,000 square feet;

Is located on a site zoned for the proposed use, as the base R1-B zoning district allows educational facilities with 
approval of a SUP;

Does not involve the use of significant amounts of hazardous substances; and

Is not located in an environmentally sensitive area, as demonstrated in the Riparian Setback Assessment 
(Attachment 11), which confirms that the on-site creek contains no riparian vegetation and does not support 
wetland habitat.
For these reasons, the proposed Project qualifies for a categorical exemption under CEQA Guidelines Section 15303.
