27.60.180 QUALIFIED (Q) OVERLAY ZONING DISTRICTS. 
(a) Q1 (Qualified Overlay District 1)—Limitations and Conditions. The following limitations 
and conditions shall pertain to the use of property zoned Q1: 
(1) Location of Structures. Permanent structures or improvements, such as parking, 
landscaping or open space may be constructed south of the ramp connecting northbound 
Highway 101 and eastbound Highway 92 only when they are not required to fulfill zoning 
requirements of adjacent properties. 
(2) Access. No additional curb cuts shall be permitted beyond those existing on the 
site as of February 1, 1987. 
(3) Residential Use. Residential use is prohibited. 
(4) Parking. Parking on this site, with the exception of the provisions of Section 
27.60.100 may be used to fulfill parking requirements for adjacent parcels. 
(5) Height Limitation. No structure shall exceed the height of the adjacent elevated 
freeway as measured to the top of the freeway railing. 
(6) Floor Area Ratio. The maximum allowed floor area ratio is 0.5. 
(b) Q2 (Qualified Overlay District 2)—Limitations and Conditions. The following limitations 
and conditions shall pertain to the use of property zoned Q2: 
(1) Lagoon Access. Public access to and along Marina Lagoon shall be provided, 
improved and maintained consistent with the Shoreline Park Specific Plan and 
requirements of the Landscape Resources Division and Public Works Department. 
(2) Parking. Parking on this site may be used to fulfill parking requirements for 
adjacent parcels. 
(3) Height Limitation. No structure shall exceed the height of the adjacent elevated 
freeway as measured to the top of the roadway railing. 
(4) Recreational vehicle storage facilities may be allowed subject to the approval of 
a special use permit under the provisions of Section 27.64.267 of this title. 
(5) Floor Area Ratio. The maximum allowed floor area ratio is 1.0. 
(c) Q3 (Qualified Overlay District 3)—Limitations and Conditions. The following limitations 
and conditions shall pertain to the use of property zoned Q3: 
243 of 409

--- page 244 ---
(1) Required Yards. A landscaped 30-foot building setback and a 15-foot parking 
setback from the edge of the shoulder of Fashion Island Boulevard shall be provided. All 
landscaping shall be subject to the approval of the Landscape Resources Division. 
(2) Access. No curb cuts shall be permitted from Fashion Island Boulevard. 
(3) Parking. Parking on this site may be used to fulfill parking requirements for 
adjacent parcels. 
(4) Height Limitation. No structure shall exceed the height of the adjacent elevated 
freeway as measured to the top of the roadway railing. 
(5) Recreational vehicle storage facilities may be allowed subject to the approval of 
a special use permit under the provisions of Section 27.64.267 of this title. 
(6) Floor Area Ratio. The maximum allowed floor area ratio is 0.5. 
(d) Q4 (Qualified Overlay District 4)—Limitations and Conditions. The following limitations 
and conditions shall pertain to the use of property zoned Q4: 
(1) Accessory Use. Parking of passenger automobiles shall be permitted only when 
accessory to abutting nonresidential uses. 
(2) Parking. Parking on the site may be used to fulfill parking requirements for 
adjacent parcels. 
(3) Height Limitation. No structure shall exceed the height of the adjacent elevated 
freeway as measured to the top of the roadway railing. 
(4) Recreational vehicle storage facilities may be allowed subject to the approval of 
a special use permit under the provisions of Section 27.64.267 of this title. 
(5) Floor Area Ratio. The maximum allowed floor area ratio is 1.0. 
(e) Q5 (Qualified Overlay District 5)—Limitations and Conditions. The following limitations 
and conditions shall pertain to the use of property zoned Q5. Q5 is the portion of the Hillsdale 
Shopping Center on the east and west side of El Camino Real (i.e., Sub-Areas A, B, C and D). 
244 of 409

--- page 245 ---
(1) Projects which involve less than 75% demolition and/or expansion and/or 
redevelopment of structures (including parking structures) in Sub-Area A or Sub-Area B or 
Sub-Area C or Sub-Area D, and which require a Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR) 
as per Section 27.08.030, will be required to meet the following findings in addition to 
findings in Section 27.08.030(a)(1)—(5): 
(A) The development facilitates the safe and efficient flow of traffic 
balanced with enhanced opportunities for public transit and a safe pedestrian 
environment along and across El Camino Real; 
(B) The development is compatible with existing retail uses, provides 
increased density of development near transit nodes, and contributes to a mix of 
uses along the corridor; 
(C) The development enhances the district's identity as a focal point along 
El Camino Real by providing high-quality architecture, landscaping and signage, 
and promoting pedestrian-oriented activity; 
(D) The development enhances the streetscape with high-quality 
landscaping sidewalks, street furniture, signage, entry features, and in the case of 
Sub-Area A, B, and D, theme intersection improvements at 31st Avenue, and 
improved connections and amenities for transit riders; and 
(E) The development promotes a healthy, vibrant business environment and 
complements the existing businesses and uses along El Camino Real. 
245 of 409

--- page 246 ---
(2) When 75% or more demolition and/or expansion and/or redevelopment of 
structures (including parking structures) occurs in Sub-Area A, B, C or D, a comprehensive 
master plan for such sub-area(s) which is consistent with the El Camino Real Master Plan 
and Hillsdale Station Area Plan is required. The development will be required to meet the 
findings in Section 27.60.160(e)(1)(i)—(v) in addition to findings in Section 27.08.030(a)(1)—
(5). 
(f) Q6 (Qualified Overlay District 6)—Limitations and Conditions. The following limitations 
and conditions shall pertain to the use of the property zoned Q6: 
(1) Uses. All uses in this district shall require a special use permit, as set forth in 
Chapter 27.74 of the Zoning Code. 
(2) Development. Future development in this district shall substantially comply with 
the conceptual development plan submitted as part of Planning Application #01-154 and 
as subsequently approved by the City Council on March 3, 2003. 
(3) Floor Area Ratio. This district shall have a maximum floor area ratio of 0.37:1. For 
the purposes of this district to calculate floor area, the size of the site is 557,568 square-
feet. 
(g) Q7 (Qualified Overlay District 7)—Limitations and Conditions. The following limitations 
and conditions shall pertain to the use of the property zoned Q7: 
(1) Uses. All uses in this district shall require a special use permit, as set forth in 
Chapter 27.74 of the Zoning Code. 
(2) Development. Future development in this district shall substantially comply with 
the St. Matthew Parish Master Plan and Special Use Permit submitted as part of Planning 
Application #10-060 and as subsequently approved by the City Council on January 22, 
2013. 
(3) Floor Area Ratio. This district shall have a maximum floor area ratio of 0.31. For 
the purposes of this district to calculate floor area, the size of the site is 310,400 square 
feet. For purposes of this zoning district, FAR will be calculated per zoning plot and not per 
parcel. 
(4) Parking. In conformance with the master plan, this district shall allow the 
establishment of 12 new parking spaces which backout directly onto Notre Dame Avenue. 
This is in addition to the 21 existing spaces that backout onto Notre Dame Avenue. 
(h) Q8 (Qualified Overlay District 8)—Limitations and Conditions.  The following limitations 
and conditions shall pertain to the use of the property zoned Q8: 
246 of 409

--- page 247 ---
(1) Uses.  All uses in this district shall require a special use permit, as set forth in 
Chapter 27.74 of the Zoning Code. 
(2) Development.  Future development in this district shall comply with the 
approved site plan and approved Special Use Permit as part of the Planning Application # 
PA2018-069 approved by the City of San Mateo.site plans and conditions of approval in all 
applicable Planning Applications. Development standards include allowance of awning up 
to nine (9) feet in height within the rear yard setback. 
(3) Floor Area Ratio.  This district shall have a maximum floor area ratio of 0.39. 
(4) Parking.  Off-site parking facilities shall not be located in excess of 1,000 feet 
from the project site. Uncovered parking may be allowed within the front and side setback 
areas. 
(4)(5)  Signage. Signage on the site shall be allowed in accordance with Title 25 of 
the San Mateo Municipal Code.

Traffic and Parking Evaluation Memorandum for 2033 La Salle Drive 
The purpose of this memorandum is to describe the approach and findings of a Traffic Evaluation for 
the proposed project at 2033 La Salle Drive (Project) in the City of San Mateo (City). The memorandum 
provides the assumptions for project understanding, data collection, and methodology of the analysis.  
Project Description 
The Project site is adjacent to residential uses and The Carey School elementary campus, located on 
La Salle Drive. The City’s designation for the site is One Family Dwelling “B” (R1B). The Carey School 
is proposing to redevelop the existing single-family residence, and an attached dwelling unit (ADU) at 
2033 La Salle Drive into an early childhood center that can accommodate up to 75 children and 16 staff 
members. It is anticipated that approximately 50% of children would carpool with a sibling that is a 
student at The Carey School. The proposed site plan is included as Attachment A.  
The Carey School’s Parking and Traffic Plan (Attachment E) includes information, policies, and 
procedures relating to traffic and parking for both the proposed early childhood center and the 
existing school campus. The Parking and Traffic Plan outlines that Project’s child drop-off/pick-up will 
occur at one of the following locations, as shown in Figure 1, depending on time of day and carpool 
situation: 
•
Early care drop-off/extended care pick-up: Park in Project parking lot and walk-in
•
Peak Period drop-off (8:00-8:25 AM)/pick-up (3:00-3:25 PM): Either at
o
Staffed carline in Project parking lot or
o
Sibling drop-off/pick-up in elementary school staffed carline on Alameda de las Pulgas
(Grades 2, 3, 5) and La Salle Drive (Grades PS, K, 1, 4). Early childhood center
students will be dropped off at the designated area for their oldest sibling. Staff will
walk children from drop-off/pickup area to building.

The Parking and Traffic Plan provides detailed procedures for each of student loading locations. For 
the Project site during off-peak period, vehicles will park in one of the parking spaces and then walk 
the child into the care center. During peak period, vehicles cannot park and will follow the drop-off and 
pick-up procedure: 
• 
From 20th Avenue, vehicles will follow one-way loop down La Salle Drive and complete full 
circle before entering Project driveway 
• 
Staff will direct vehicles into designated loading spot and will supervise children 
entering/exiting the vehicle 
• 
Vehicles will exit project site and head north towards 20th Avenue  
TRIP GENERATION 
The standard practice of starting an assessment of transportation related elements for new projects is 
to evaluate what the multi-modal transportation (vehicle, bike, and pedestrian) change may include.  A 
trip generation analysis was conducted to determine the number of trips the Project would generate. 
The trip generation was determined based on average rates from Institute of Transportation Engineer’s 
(ITE) publication, Trip Generation, 11th Edition.

For the proposed early childhood center, ITE Land Use 565: Day Care Center was used. Note Trip 
Generation does not provide trip generation data during the School PM for both the existing and the 
proposed land uses, therefore as a conservative approach the commute PM trip generation rates were 
used instead. Also, ITE Trip Generation Vehicle Time of Day Distribution tables reports that 
approximately 6.6% of daily residential trips (1 trip) and 4.3% of daily day care trips (13 trips) occur 
during the School PM peak hour of 2:00 and 3:00 PM.  
For the proposed use, a carpool trip reduction was applied because approximately 50% of students of 
proposed childhood center have a sibling that attends the existing elementary school and would arrive 
in the same vehicle. As a conservative approach, this percentage was determined based on the lowest 
observed percentage in the 6 most recent school years of an existing off-site childhood center currently 
operated by the applicant, as shown in Figure 2. Note that the 6-year average is closer to 60%. The 
sibling carpool trips will utilize the existing Carey School drop off and pick up areas at Alameda de las 
Pulgas and La Salle and then walk to the Project.

TRIP ASSIGNMENT 
As shown in Table 1, it is anticipated that during the peak hours approximately 29 trips will utilize the 
staff car line in the Project parking lot and the remaining 30 trips will utilize the sibling loading areas 
on Alameda de Las Pulgas or La Salle Drive shown inFigure 1. It is assumed that 95% of net new 
trips will come from the west of W 20th Avenue and La Salle Dr, while the remaining 5% of trips will 
come from the east. 
Level of Transportation Analysis 
As of July 1, 2020, the State of California has fully adopted a change in the California Environmental 
Quality Act (CEQA) significant impact methodology for transportation impacts to use vehicle miles 
traveled (VMT) as opposed to level of service (LOS) via State Bill 743 (SB 743). To address this change, 
the City of San Mateo developed and adopted the Transportation Impact Analysis Guidelines (TIA 
Guidelines) to provide screening criteria for determination of the level of transportation analysis and 
requirements for a transportation analysis. 
Transportation analysis may consist of analysis required by CEQA and/or supplemental non-CEQA 
Local Transportation Analysis (LTA). The City’s TIA Guidelines outline criteria for determining the level 
of transportation analysis for a given project.  
CEQA Screening 
A project may be exempt from performing CEQA analysis if the project meets at least one screening 
criteria based on: 
• 
Small Project 
• 
Affordable Housing 
• 
Local-Serving Retail and Public Services 
• 
High-Quality Transit Area (HQTA) 
• 
Consistency with RTP/SCS 
The Project is determined to be exempted from CEQA analysis as summarized in Table 2. This 
determination is made based on the Local-Serving Retail and Public Services screening criteria. Based 
on the current Project information given for this analysis, a presumption of less than significance can 
be made and no VMT analysis is required. Detailed evaluation for each criterion is discussed in the 
following sections.

Small Project 
Small projects are defined as projects that generate less than 110 daily vehicle trips. An average of 
110 average daily trips roughly equates to: 
• 
10 single family residential units 
• 
11 multifamily residential units 
• 
11,000 square feet of office 
As shown in Table 1, the Project generates a net new 133 daily trips, which is greater than the 110-
vehicle trip threshold and does not satisfy this criterion.  
Affordable Housing 
Project components which consist of 100 percent deed restricted affordable housing may be exempt. 
The project does not include any components that fit this description.   
Local-service Retail and Public Services 
Projects that are locally serving retail equal or less than 50,000 square feet may be exempt. The City’s 
guidelines determine local serving retail based on location, characteristics, and envision goods and 
services the retail development would provide. The goods and services provided would be something 
people would need on a regular basis and be close to where people live. Some examples in the City’s 
guidelines include groceries, medicines, restaurants, and fitness and beauty services.  
Based on the City’s guidelines, the childcare service provided by the Project is considered as local 
serving since the Project is located in a residential area of the City and the provided service needed on 
a daily weekday basis. Since the Project is a local service less than 50,000 square, it may be screened 
out from further VMT analysis.  
High-Quality Transit Area (HQTA) 
Locations within high-quality transit area, and/or near Caltrain stations, may be screened out. Figure 3 
illustrates the HQTA within the City, which does not include the Project vicinity, therefore the Project 
does not satisfy this screening criterion.  
Projects Located in Low VMT Areas 
Residential and employment projects within areas that generate VMT below adopted City thresholds 
can be screened out from further VMT analysis. The VMT per capita and VMT per employee are shown 
in the San Mateo Transportation Impact Guidelines. Figures in Attachment B of San Mateo 
Transportation Impact Guidelines show that existing VMT are higher than the City’s thresholds and 
therefore could not be screened out.

Local Transportation Analysis 
A non-CEQA local transportation analysis (LTA) may be required to evaluate the effects of the 
development project on the circulation network in proximity of the project site. LTA for the project may 
include the following analysis and evaluations: 
• 
Traffic operation analysis 
• 
Site Review

Site access and circulation

PROJECT TRAFFIC OPERATION 
The Carey School’s Parking and Traffic Plan (Attachment E) includes information, policies, and 
procedures relating to traffic and parking for both the proposed early childhood center and the 
existing school campus. The plan is shared with parents and students each year with reminders sent 
out regularly.  
The Parking and Traffic Plan outlines that Project’s child drop-off/pick-up will occur at one of three (3) 
student locations, shown in Figure 1, depending on time of day and carpool situation. For vehicles 
accessing the Project site during off-peak period, vehicles will park in one of the parking spaces and 
then walk the child into the care center. During peak period, vehicles cannot park and will follow the 
drop-off and pick-up procedure: 
• 
From 20th Avenue, vehicles will follow one-way loop down La Salle Drive and complete full 
circle before entering Project driveway 
• 
Staff will direct vehicles into designated loading spot and will supervise children 
entering/exiting the vehicle 
• 
Vehicles will exit project site and head north towards 20th Avenue  
Carpool vehicles will utilize the sibling drop-off/pick-up in elementary school staffed carline on 
Alameda de las Pulgas (Grades 2, 3, 5) or La Salle Drive (Grades PS, K, 1, 4). Early childhood center 
students will be dropped off at the designated area for their oldest sibling. Staff will walk children from 
drop-off/pickup area to building. 
TRAFFIC OPERATION ANALYSIS 
Traffic operation analysis was conducted for the unsignalized intersection of W 20th Avenue and La 
Salle Drive during the AM, School PM, and commute PM peak hours. The traffic analysis utilized traffic 
counts that were collected on Thursday, September 4th, 2025 during the AM (7-9 AM), school PM (2-4 
PM), and the commute PM peak (4-6 PM) peak periods when school (including the existing elementary 
campus) was in session. Raw counts are included in Attachment B.

The intersection level of service (LOS) and queuing were conducted to determine the potential change 
in traffic operation at the study intersection. LOS for the intersection was determined using the Highway 
Capacity Manual 7th Edition (HCM 7) methodology within Synchro 12 software. For side street stop 
control (SSSC) intersections, HCM methodology defines LOS as a function of the average control delay 
for the worst minor street movement/approach or major street left-turn. The results are presented below 
in Table 3. The analysis indicates the intersection performs at an acceptable LOS C or better for all 
peak periods. It is anticipated that the Project will increase delay by 1.6 second per vehicle or less. 
Synchro outputs are included in Attachment C.

Queues were also determined using the Highway Capacity Manual 7th Edition (HCM 7) methodology 
within Synchro 12 software. Similar to LOS, HCM 7 methodology reports queue lengths for the worst 
minor street movement/approach or major street left-turn. HCM 7 outputs reports queues by the number 
of vehicles and were converted to feet assuming 25 feet per vehicle.  
The results are presented below in Table 4. The analysis indicates the queue lengths were all at most 
one vehicle during all peak periods. It is anticipated that the Project will not increase any existing queues 
by more than one vehicle, or 25 feet. Synchro outputs are included in Attachment C.

PLAN REVIEW 
Site Circulation 
As discussed in the Project Description section and school’s Parking and Traffic Plan, childcare drop-
off and pick-up operation will differ depending on time of day. During off-peak period, vehicles will park 
in one of the parking spaces and then walk the child into the care center. During peak periods, vehicles 
cannot park in the Project’s parking lot and drop-off/pick-up operations will occur at the staffed carline 
within the Project’s parking lot or sibling drop-off at the staffed carline for the adjacent elementary school 
on Alameda de las Pulgas. The drop-off and pickup activities will be grouped in distinct 15-minute 
schedules to best manage the safety and efficiency of these operations. The Carey School will monitor 
these activities and make adjustments for improvements if needed. 
Student Loading Queue 
A student loading queue analysis was conducted to determine if the proposed loading area for the early 
childhood center would be adequate during a 25-minute peak during the morning drop-off and afternoon 
pick-up periods. The queue for the existing elementary campus was not evaluated as the Project will 
not increase the number of vehicles for that site. The queuing analysis compared the arrival and 
departure rates for the loading queue. 
260 of 409

--- page 261 ---
Page 12 
kimley-horn.com 
4637 Chabot Drive, Suite 300, Pleasanton, CA 94588 
925-398-4840 
 
 
During peak morning and afternoon peak periods, non-carpool students will utilize the staff carline 
within the Project parking lot. It is assumed that approximately 50 feet (2 vehicles) between the entry 
and exit drive aisles may be used for student loading activity and approximately 45 feet (2 vehicles) 
could queue in the entry throat before spilling onto La Salle Drive. This equates to overall vehicle 
storage of 4 vehicles, where 2 vehicles for loading activities and 2 vehicles for waiting. 
 
As a conservative approach, the arrival rate assumed that all peak hour vehicles would arrive with in 
linear distribution within the 25-minute peak period. Note Trip Generation defines trip as a one 
directional movement, therefore the number of vehicles was the maximum between the inbound or 
outbound trips.  For both peak periods, it is estimated the average arrival rate of 0.6 vehicles per minute 
(veh/min). 
 
The departure rate was determined based on average drop-off and pick-up dwelling times and active 
loading queue storage. Based on engineering and professional judgment, conservative estimates for 
average drop-off and pick-up dwelling times of 4 minutes (240 seconds) were used in the analysis. The 
drop-off/pick-up time is the assumed amount of time it takes for a vehicle to enter a temporary curb-
side space and for children to safely exit or enter the car. For both peak periods, it is estimated the 
average departure rate of 0.5 veh/min. 
The results of the student loading queues are summarized in Table 5. Since the arrival rate is greater 
than the departure rate, there will be an unserved rate of 0.1 veh/min which equates to approximately 
2.5 vehicle queue (unserved rate multiplied by 25-minute peak period). The queue analysis calculation 
is included in Attachment D. 
To minimize queues spillover, a sensitivity analysis was conducted to determine the average dwelling 
time which would result in two-vehicle queue, one-vehicle queue, or no queue in the entry throat. The 
results of the sensitivity analysis are presented in Table 6 where the average dwelling times ranged 
from 3.8 minute (230 seconds) for two-vehicle queue to 3.3 minutes (200 seconds) for no queue. As 
stated previously, The Carey School will monitor these activities and make adjustments for 
improvements if needed.

Parking Assessment 
The Project will provide 11 parking spaces on-site. In addition, The Carey School has a shared parking 
agreement where it leases a total of 45 parking spaces, where 15 spaces will be dedicated to the 
proposed early childhood center, from the buildings at 1900-2000 Alameda de las Pulgas. The parking 
lease term runs from March 1, 2025, through March 31, 2030, with options for extension.   
For on-site parking, one (1) space will be dedicated to the Director and all remaining Staff will utilize 
the remote parking spaces at 1900-2000 Almeda de las Pulgas. The remaining ten (10) spaces will be 
utilized for parent drop-off and pick-up, outside of the staffed carline operations noted in the section 
above. 
Parking requirements for the proposed Project are presented in Chapter 27.64.160 of San Mateo’s 
Municipal Code. For day nurseries, including preschools and nursery schools, the minimum parking 
required includes: 
• 
1 space for each employee. 
• 
Designated spaces for loading and unloading children, where 1 space per 6 persons (or portion 
thereof) licensed at the facility with maximum of 3 spaces for up to 30 licensed persons, and 
thereafter 1 space per 10 licensed person. 
o 
The loading/unloading spaces may be located on street frontage with appropriate 
permits for loadings zones. 
o 
The overall requirement may be reduced by 1 space by the provision of a permanently 
assigned employee to assist children from the drop-off area to the facility.  
Table 7 summarizes the parking requirement for the Project, which is 23 spaces. The combined total 
of on-site parking and remote parking equates to 26 spaces, which satisfies the City’s requirements. It 
should be noted that this analysis does not include spaces for the staffed carline on Alameda de las 
Pulgas or La Salle Drive, reflecting a conservative approach to the drop-off and pick-up operations.

Parking analysis also evaluated if the parking inventory for the building located at 1900-2000 Alameda 
de las Pulgas would remain sufficient after leasing 45 spaces to The Carey School. The 1900 Alameda 
Building is evaluated based on the R&D parking requirements noted in the City’s parking requirements. 
This evaluation is based on the City’s record of improvements starting in year 2020 for Speculative Lab 
and Support Spaces completed for the 1900 Alameda building, under Building Permit BD-2020-275487 
and subsequent improvement permits for all the leasable space. Based on the 1900 Alameda use as 
Laboratory and 1950 and 2000 Alameda uses as Office, the combined minimum parking requirement 
would result in 713 parking spaces. This parking space requirement is assuming a 100% occupancy of 
the buildings rather than reflective of a specific tenant occupancy percentage, which would be less than 
100% due to hybrid schedules for many employers in the regions. The 1900-2000 Alameda buildings 
provide 801 parking spaces, inclusive of a 430-space parking structure and a 371-space surface lot. 
The shared use of all parking spaces was documented as a Declaration of Covenants, Conditions and 
Restrictions (CC&R’s) recorded on June 6, 1984, as Instrument No 1984-061165 with the County of 
San Mateo. 
In summary, the inventory of 801 parking spaces allows for a sufficient supply of the 713 required 
Office/R&D parking, as well as the 45 spaces leased to The Carey School, leaving a surplus of 43 
spaces available. Table 8 summarizes the calculation of these results.

CONCLUSION 
The following is a summary of the traffic and parking evaluation: 
Project Description 
•
The Project site is located at 2033 La Salle Drive, which is adjacent to residential uses and 
The Carey School elementary campus.
•
The Project is proposing to redevelop the existing single-family residence and an attached 
dwelling unit (ADU) into an early childhood center that can accommodate up to 75 children. It 
is anticipated that approximately 50% of children would carpool with a sibling that is a student 
at The Carey School.
•
The proposed project will generate a net new 133 daily trips, 28 net new trips in the AM peak 
hour, 27 net new trips in the School PM peak hour, and 27 net new trips in the PM peak hour.
Vehicle Miles Traveled 
•
The Project is determined to be exempted from CEQA analysis based on the Local-Serving
Retail and Public Services screening criteria.
Traffic Operation 
•
Level of service analysis found that the intersection of W 20th Avenue and La Salle Drive will
operate at LOS C or better during the AM, School PM, and commute PM peak hours with the
addition of Project traffic
•
Queuing analysis found that the Project will not increase any existing queues by more than
one vehicles or 25 feet.
•
The results of the traffic analysis found that the Project would result in minimal impact to
existing operations.
Plan Review 
•
Childcare drop-off and pick-up operation will differ depending on time of day.
o
During the Project’s peak hour, drop-off/pickup operations will occur at the staffed
carline within the Project’s parking lot or sibling drop-off at the staffed carline for the
adjacent elementary school on Alameda de las Pulgas.
o
During non-peak times, vehicles may park in the Project parking lot and walk-in.
o
The Carey School will monitor these activities and make adjustments for
improvements if needed.
•
Student loading found that staff carline would need to have an average dwell time of less
than 4 minutes to ensure that queues do not spill onto La Salle Drive during peak periods.
•
The combined total on-site parking and off-site parking equates to 26 spaces, which satisfies
the City’s requirements of 23 spaces.

Attachment E – The Carey School’s Parking and Traffic Plan

The Carey School’s Parking and Traffic Plan  
This plan has been updated to include the proposed Carey School Early Childhood Center 
(ECC) on La Salle Drive into Carey’s existing Parking and Traffic Plan. This plan, including on 
designated pick-up and drop-off locations, traffic flow, and escort requirements, is shared with 
the Carey Community each year and reminders are sent regularly to require all community 
members to follow the plan as outlined below. The requirements of this plan will be monitored 
by Carey’s Head of School, Director of Operations and Director of Facilities. 
One of our primary responsibilities as neighborhood community members is to execute a safe 
and efficient parking and traffic plan. The plan that follows is one we have developed in 
collaboration with the City of San Mateo and our neighbors. The principal goals of the plan are 
two: 
1.​ To ensure the safety of the children, the school community, and those in the 
neighborhood. 
2.​ To create an efficient flow of traffic to minimize the traffic impact on the neighborhood 
for daily school operations and special events. 
We appreciate all you do to maintain good relationships with our neighbors, and therefore, we 
require your full adherence to this plan at all times. 
A. Staggered Start and End Times 
The school has early morning care beginning at 7:45 am and extended care each afternoon until 
6:00 pm. We ask that you utilize the chart below for the location and drop-off and pick-up 
times of each grade: 
Grade

*Note: If you have more than one child in the school, please use the designated area/time for 
the oldest child.  
B. Staffing 
●​
During peak morning times, there will be five administrators at drop-off and pick-up 
areas (on the Alameda and on the La Salle circle), and one staff member on the corner 
of 20th Ave and La Salle (denoted by the numeral 5) from 8:00-8:25 am and 3:00-3:30 
pm to assist children and to help direct the flow of traffic. Please see the exhibits of the 
La Salle circle below where the numbers denote administrator on duty.  
●​
During peak afternoon times, each lead and assistant teacher for grades will supervise 
the pick-up for the respective grades. 
●​
All school staff on duty use walkie talkies to communicate and create a safe and efficient 
process.  
Note: Additionally, the administrators on duty will help ensure that the driveways are free for 
neighbor use (driveways denoted on exhibit with X). On rare occasions, when a car in the 
queue blocks the flow of traffic, they will be asked to drive around the block.  
C. Preschool Student Logistics 
*The following logistics apply to all locations preschool students are dropped off and picked up 
(La Salle, Alameda, ECC parking lot) 
●​
Preschool students with siblings should be dropped off and picked up with their oldest 
sibling 
●​
To ensure safe exit and entrance of cars on La Salle and Alameda, preschool students 
should be seated closest to the rear passenger door so staff can ensure their safe exit 
and entrance to vehicles. 
●​
School staff shall be assigned to escort all preschool students from all designated pick-up 
locations on La Salle and the Alameda to the school building, and from the building back 
to each pick-up location. 
One Carey School Lane • San Mateo, CA 94403 • Phone (650) 345-8205 • Fax (650) 345-2528 • www.careyschool.org 
 
287 of 409

--- page 288 ---
●​
While assigned staff are escorting students to or from the building, another staff 
member shall remain stationed at each drop-off and pick-up location to receive arriving 
preschool students and ensure continuous supervision. Each location must always have 
at least one dedicated staff member present during the entire pick-up and drop-off 
period. 
●​
Students shall be escorted by school staff or parents/guardians between the 2033 La 
Salle parking lot and the school building. Unaccompanied students are not permitted to 
walk between these areas. 
D. Traffic Procedures La Salle (Grades PS, K, 1, 4) 
All vehicles are required to drive slowly on La Salle, when turning off of and returning to 20th 
Ave.   
 
*Numbers in exhibit are personnel locations 
Rules of the Road: 
One Carey School Lane • San Mateo, CA 94403 • Phone (650) 345-8205 • Fax (650) 345-2528 • www.careyschool.org 
 
288 of 409

--- page 289 ---
●​
Please do not park on the La Salle Circle during peak hours as it is used for drop-off and 
pick-up. 
●​
Pull all the way forward on La Salle by completing the full circle around the cul-de-sac.  
The forward-most drop-off and pick-up location would be just beyond the school’s 
driveway. 
●​
In order to ensure safe access and egress to and from the neighborhood, please stay in 
your vehicle at all times and follow the flow of traffic and do not leave the line to turn 
back around, especially by using a neighbor’s driveway. 
●​
Staff will direct cars into each designated drop-off/pick-up spot in the circle and 
supervise children entering/exiting the vehicle. 
●​
Families and faculty/staff are asked not to park on La Salle during the school day. If you 
need to come to campus, utilize parking on the Alameda, in the ECC parking lot, 2000 
Alameda or short-term parking in the circle outside of carline operation.  
E. Traffic Procedures Alameda (Grades 2, 3, 5) 
All vehicles are required to drive slowly on the Alameda into the white zone. The School 
maintains a speed limit monitor to encourage drivers to maintain a safe speed.  Be advised that 
parking will not be allowed from the end of the white zone to the end of the red zone fire 
hydrant on the Alameda from 2:30 pm – 3:30 pm. 
 
*Numbers in exhibit are personnel locations 
Rules of the Road: 
One Carey School Lane • San Mateo, CA 94403 • Phone (650) 345-8205 • Fax (650) 345-2528 • www.careyschool.org 
 
289 of 409

--- page 290 ---
●​
The white zone in front of the school is designated as a drop-off/pick-up zone only.  
Please do not park in this area. 
●​
In order to ensure the safety of passenger cars behind you, please stay in your vehicle at 
all times and pull all the way forward on the Alameda to the forward-most spot in the 
white zone (Note that this spot is several car lengths in front of the front gate). 
●​
Staff will direct cars into each designated drop-off/pick-up spot in the white zone and 
supervise children entering/exiting the vehicle. 
F. Early Childhood Center Drop-Off and Pick-Up 
 
*Numbers in exhibit are personnel locations 
 
Rules of the Road: 
●​
Pull all the way forward on La Salle, complete the full circle and then pull into the ECC 
driveway.  Pull as far forward as possible in the drop-off lane to keep traffic flowing.  
One Carey School Lane • San Mateo, CA 94403 • Phone (650) 345-8205 • Fax (650) 345-2528 • www.careyschool.org 
 
290 of 409

--- page 291 ---
●​
Staff will direct cars into each designated drop-off/pick-up spot in the parking lot and 
supervise children entering/exiting the vehicle. Remain in your car unless directed 
otherwise by staff.  
●​
In order to ensure safe access and egress to and from the neighborhood, please follow 
the one-way loop from W 20th Ave down La Salle Dr through the drop-off loop and do 
not jump the line, follow the flow of traffic. If dropping off, have your child signed in on 
Procare and have their backpacks and belongings ready to speed up unloading. 
F. Extended Care Drop-Off and Pick-Up During Non-Peak Times 
School is open as of 7:45 am and those dropping off before 8:00 am must walk students to the 
gate where they are monitored upon entry to the premises. The Alameda (non-white zone) and 
La Salle cul-de-sac are available for parking during these times. When picking up your student 
from extended care, please park parallel on Alameda or in the ECC parking lot.  The faculty 
parking lot is not available for parent parking unless otherwise specified (see Special Events). 
G. Special Events 
The School has established parking routines for special events are tailored to the anticipated 
parking need of the particular event in an effort to minimize the impact on the neighborhood.  
For nighttime events, the campus grounds may be used for parking, which increases the onsite 
spaces by 30.  The school partners with the commercial property at 2000 Alameda to handle 
overflow parking or for parents that wish to park and walk their children into school.  
H. Contacting the School 
In the event you have observations or concerns about the parking or traffic conditions near The 
Carey School, please contact Head of School, Neely Norris at (650) 345-8205 or send an email 
to nnorris@careyschool.org.   
I. Help the Environment 
To relieve traffic and to help the environment, we encourage the following modes of 
transportation to and from school: 
●​ Walk/Bike to School: The Carey School Bi-Ped Club - Contact The Carey School for 
more information. 
 
●​ Carpool to School: School Pools - The School maintains a GoKid account which is a 
convenient and reliable school carpooling program for schools which helps families form 
One Carey School Lane • San Mateo, CA 94403 • Phone (650) 345-8205 • Fax (650) 345-2528 • www.careyschool.org 
 
291 of 409

--- page 292 ---
and manage carpools. ​
 
Also, when in the queue, turn your car off if you will be waiting for more than a minute.  Idling 
wastes gas and causes more pollution than restarting your car. 
Thank you for your assistance in making The Carey School safe and for being a 
responsible community member. 
If you have any questions about these protocols, please contact Neely Norris, Head of School at 
nnorris@careyschool.org or (650)345-2044. 
One Carey School Lane • San Mateo, CA 94403 • Phone (650) 345-8205 • Fax (650) 345-2528 • www.careyschool.org

Memorandum 
 
October 29, 2025 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Project # 4907-01 
 
To:  
Michelle Huber, StudioBondy Architecture; Mara Chase, Carey School  
 
 
 
From:  
Kelly Hardwicke, H. T. Harvey & Associates  
 
 
Subject:  
Riparian Setback Assessment for Early Childhood Center for Carey Schoool 
Project, City of San Mateo, San Mateo County, California  
 
 
 
Executive Summary. This memorandum was prepared to document the appropriate riparian setback for a 
construction of a new Early Childhood Center for Carey School at 1 Carey School Lane in the City of San Mateo. 
The Early Childhood Center (project) would be located at an adjacent parcel, at 2033 LaSalle Drive, Assessor’s 
Parcel Number (APN)-039040080 (Figure 1). An unnamed creek serves as the property line between the 2033 
LaSalle Drive project parcel and Carey School. This memorandum summarizes the habitat characteristics of the 
unnamed creek and riparian corridor located along the north edge of the creek, and provides our opinion of the 
appropriate, San Mateo-required riparian setback. The project parcel was evaluated by qualified biologists to 
determine the limits of sensitive riparian habitat within the unnamed creek, the TOB, and also to evaluate the 
potential for impacts to this habitat from the project. Using this data, setbacks appropriate to City codes were 
established (Figure 2), and new project buildings will entirely avoid these setbacks. No riparian trees will be 
removed by the project, and there will be no encroachment into riparian habitat beyond the existing development. 
The project is expected to have only minor, temporary, self restoring impacts to riparian habitat and no impacts 
to the creek itself.  
 
Regulatory Setting. The City of San Mateo has a city-wide setback requirement for waterways, Municipal Code 
7.39.130: Watercourse Protection (City of San Mateo 2024)1. Development setback from the unnamed creek was 
determined as described in Municipal Code 7.39.130 (a) and (b)(3). Additionally, our riparian setback assessment 
evaluated the riparian setback from the unnamed creek in accordance with the slope setback requirements 
applicable to stream banks described in City of San Mateo Slope Development Standards, pages 2-6 (City of San 
Mateo 1998).2 We have also mapped and discussed the minimal and less than significant potential impacts to 
 
1 City of San Mateo. 2024. City of San Mateo Municipal Code, City of San Mateo Law Library. Accessed at: 
https://law.cityofsanmateo.org/us/ca/cities/san-mateo/code in November 2024 
2 City of San Mateo. 1998. Slope Development Standards: Questions and Answers about Building on Sloped Property. 
Available from https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/DocumentCenter/View/92653/Slope-Development-Standards 
314 of 409

--- page 315 ---
2 
H. T. Harvey & Associates 
sensitive riparian habitat associated with the unnamed stream, which are typically analyzed under CEQA 
Appendix G, Biological Resources Guideline B, which covers impacts to riparian habitat and other sensitive 
natural communities.  
 
Methods. H. T. Harvey & Associates plant and wetland ecologist Katherine Marlin, M.S., conducted a 
reconnaissance-level survey of the project site, defined as parcel 039040080 on October 30, 2024. The purpose 
of the survey was to provide creek and riparian habitat mapping, including top of bank and riparian dripline, and 
to measure various creek dimensions such as average depth and horizontal bank distance to apply the correct 
slope setback methods. We also mapped the location of top of bank (TOB), as well as the riparian dripline on 
the north bank of the creek, using sub-meter GPS. Creek depth was estimated using an inclinometer and verified 
using ESRI’s aggregated topographic LIDAR data for the area (ESRI, 2024).   Top of bank was mapped for the 
northern creek bank using methods from A Field Guide to the Identification of the Ordinary High Water Mark (OHWM) 
in the Arid West Region of the Western United States: A Delineation Manual (USACE 2008).3 
 
Within the riparian dripline and creek banks, we mapped sensitive riparian habitat. Riparian habitat was mapped 
based on the canopy line of trees rooted within TOB and changes in the vegetative community, from the 
understory species described in the preceding paragraph, to planted, ornamental species. Riparian habitat would 
also include all areas below the TOB. However, it should be noted that the areas underneath the riparian canopy 
that overhang TOB at this site were developed as yard and ornamental vegetation, and would be considered 
developed beyond TOB. Observations of the creek conditions and habitats were also noted. TOB was recorded 
by flagging the TOB in the field and then surveying this line in using accurate survey methods.  
 
City of San Mateo Municipal Code 7.39.130: WATERCOURSE PROTECTION applies to all watercourses, 
public and private, throughout the city (City of San Mateo 2024).  Therefore, our setback analysis focused on the 
WATERCOURSE PROTECTION code and the City’s Slope Development Standards, which apply to creek 
banks. 
 
In accordance with the City of San Mateo Municipal Code 7.39.130: WATERCOURSE PROTECTION, under 
Chapter 7.39: Stormwater Management and Discharge (City of San Mateo 2024):  
 
“(a) Every person owning property through which a watercourse passes, or such person's lessee or 
tenant, shall keep and maintain that part of the watercourse within the property reasonably free of 
trash, debris, excessive vegetation, and other obstacles which would pollute, contaminate, or 
significantly retard the flow of water through the watercourse; shall maintain existing privately owned 
structures within or adjacent to a watercourse, so that such structures will not become a hazard to the 
use, function, or physical integrity of the watercourse; and shall not remove healthy bank vegetation 
beyond that actually necessary for said maintenance, nor remove said vegetation in such a manner as to 
increase the vulnerability of the watercourse to erosion. 
 
 
 
3 [USACE] U.S. Army Corps of Engineers. 2008. A Field Guide to the Identification of the Ordinary High Water Mark 
(OHWM) in the Arid West Region of the Western United States: A Delineation Manual. ERDC/CRREL TR-08-12. 
315 of 409

--- page 316 ---
3 
H. T. Harvey & Associates 
(b) No person shall commit or cause to be committed any of the following acts, unless a written permit 
has first been obtained from the Director of Public Works: 
 
… (3) Carry out development within 30 feet of the center line of any creek or 20 feet of the 
top of a bank; …or,  
 
(6) Place any loose or unconsolidated material along the side of or within a watercourse or so 
close to the side as to cause a diversion of the flow, or to cause a probability of such material 
being carried away by stormwaters passing through such watercourse.”  
 
 
City of San Mateo Slope Development Standards state that the slope setback distance is determined by a 
combination of slope steepness, slope height at top of slope, and/or a calculation of distance related to slope 
height and horizonal/vertical distance (City of San Mateo 1998). As per the Slope Development Standards:  
 
“for a slope over 25% up to and including 50%, and 10 feet to 30 feet height top of slope, the setback 
from top of slope is the greater of either: 
 
15 feet,  
 
The diagonal distance of 3:1, 3 horizontal to 1 vertical measured from the toe slope, or,  
 
A distance equal to the slope height from the top of slope.”  
 
In this case, we defined “toe slope” to be the bottom of the creek, which was approximated well by the current 
property line which is a stream centerline, and “top of slope” to be TOB.  
 
We chose three points along the creek which each represent approximately 1/3 of the length of the creek, each 
with unique characteristics including ground cover and slope percent. Then, using an inclinometer, we measured 
degree of slope steepness from the toe of slope. Horizontal distance from toe of slope to top of slope/bank was 
measured using GPS. Finally, the depth from toe of slope to the bottom of the creek was visually estimated  and 
trigonometric calculations, and verified using LIDAR topographic data (ESRI, 2024). 
 
Results. The approximately 0.6-acre project parcel is located in the midst of urban-suburban development, 3.5 
miles east of Crystal Springs and 4 miles west of the San Francisco Bay (Figure 1). The reach of the unnamed 
creek adjacent to the parcel is channelized and runs perpendicular to LaSalle Drive. The creek does not appear in 
maps from National Wetlands Inventory or U.S. Geological Survey, and is undergrounded in culverts and bridges 
both up- and down-stream of the project site. At the time of the October survey, there was low flow with about 
3-6 inches of water. Since October is towards the end of the dry season, and the conditions were normal at the 
time of the survey, this unnamed creek is likely perennial (EPA 2024).4 The creek channel is incised, likely due to 
high flows during previous rainy seasons’ storm events. There is a three-foot-wide culvert at the west end of the 
unnamed creek, a chain-link fence near the midway point with a handmade structure that allows for water flow, 
 
4 [EPA] Environmental Protection Agency. 2024. Antecedent Precipitation Tool [Software]. Available from https:// 
www.epa.gov/wotus/antecedent-precipitation-tool-apt. 
 
316 of 409

--- page 317 ---
4 
H. T. Harvey & Associates 
and an opening at the east end which drains under the road. The eastern drainage is piped underground after the 
road crossing. The low-flow channel is approximately 3 feet wide and has a sandy substrate filled with 3-4 inch 
wide, gravelly rocks. The creek bottom is unvegetated, does not support wetlands, and tree roots stick out of the 
break in slope delimiting the low flow channel.  
 
The mapped TOB line and riparian canopy and habitat are shown on Figure 2. The riparian area within the project 
parcel was determined by identifying trees rooted below or right at the top of bank on the 2033 LaSalle Drive 
side of the creek, and whose canopies overhung the creek substantially. Riparian habitat did not include any trees 
rooted beyond top of bank, even if they had continuous canopy cover with trees rooted below top of bank, as 
many of these appeared planted and did not have any biological relation to the stream, being located well above 
the stream’s water table or expected area of normal flooding. The riparian area within the parcel has an 
approximately 50% slope (2:1). The slopes are more gradual at the east and west extremities, and steepest in the 
middle. Overstory tree species included some natives such as coast live oak (Quercus agrifolia) and cottonwood 
(Populus fremontii), as well as non-natives such as Japanese cheesewood (Pittosporum tobira), brush cherry (Syzygium 
paniculatum), silky oak (Grevillea robusta), and Peruvian pepper tree (Schinus molle). A planted coast redwood (Sequoia 
sempervirens) was rooted just above the edge of top of bank at the eastern reach and is not considered a part of the 
riparian drip line. This redwood is a part of a continuous row of landscaped yard trees that are planted in a flat, 
sandy landscaped area. Understory vegetation species included nightshade (Solanum sp.), smooth leaved elm 
(Ulmus minor), bitter lettuce (Lactuca virosa), French broom (Genista monspessulana), Himalayan blackberry (Rubus 
armeniacus), bull thistle (Cirsium vulgare), nettleleaf goosefoot (Chenopodium murale), periwinkle (Vinca major), English 
ivy (Hedera helix), and stream orchid (Epipactis sp.), all of which were vegetative at the time of the survey.  
 
Upland, developed habitat north of the riparian habitat was flat and entirely developed/landscaped, consisting of 
concrete driveway, ornamental species such as aloe (Aloe sp.), or jade (Crassula sp.), turf grasses, and redwoods 
along the east edge of the parcel. Developed plantings occurred under the riparian dripline beyond TOB and 
would not be considered sensitive habitat at the ground level, even though the riparian canopy overhangs this 
area. Photos of the creek channel, riparian area, and adjacent upland are presented in Appendix B. 
 
Stream/Slope Setback. Slope height was 10, 8.5, and 7 feet at data points 1, 2 and 3 respectively. The average 
vertical slope height at top of slope/bank was 8.5 feet. Therefore, the minimum slope setback for new buildings, 
as described in the Slope Development Standards, is 15 feet from TOB. This is greater than either the 3:1 distance 
from toe of slope or the distance of the depth from TOB.   
 
The Watercourse Setback was evaluated as 20 feet from TOB, which was greater than 30 feet from toe of slope. 
Figure 2 in Appendix A shows the results from the survey on October 30, 2024, including TOB, stream 
centerline/toe of slope, dripline for the north bank riparian vegetation, and the slope and watercourse setbacks. 
New buildings proposed by the project avoid both setbacks.  
 
Riparian Impacts under CEQA. The proposed project associated with this riparian setback survey is 
anticipated to have less than significant impacts on the riparian area and no impacts on the creek itself. The 
317 of 409

--- page 318 ---
5 
H. T. Harvey & Associates 
proposed project will not be removing any riparian trees or trees within the riparian corridor, and has been 
designed to avoid all impacts to the creek, creek banks, and riparian corridor. Tree protection zones will be 
established around all trees to be preserved by the project, with arborist monitoring for work that must occur 
within these zones. Project activities are planned as replacement-in-kind within the existing developed footprint. 
However, any development that may occur under the riparian canopy that overhangs the site will only affect the 
existing developed habitat, and will not introduce new buildings within this area. Within the developed area under 
the overhanging riparian canopy and adjacent to this area within the setback, existing landscaping will be updated 
for landscaping consistent with the requirements of the Early Childhood Center, such as garden nooks, a 
vegetable garden and sand and mud play areas. There would be no new hardscape under the riparian canopy and 
no increase in hardscape within the setback area from existing conditions.  
 
Implementation of the proposed project could result in temporary impacts to the adjacent mixed riparian 
woodland habitat (i.e., trimming of riparian trees or minor impacts to roots) as a result of construction in the 
landscaped urban-suburban strip along the riparian canopy edge (Figure 2), however these impacts are expected 
to be minor, would restore naturally after construction, and would not constitute a permanent reduction in 
riparian canopy. During construction, the riparian trees and the sensitive areas below TOB would be protected 
with appropriate Best Management Practices (BMPs), which may include fiber rolls and Environmentally 
Sensitive Area fencing. The project would not be expected to introduce additional human presence within the 
riparian habitat, as there are no plans for the Center to utilize, develop, or in any other way permanently impact 
the riparian habitat or creek. Given the existing levels of disturbance, the replacement of existing landscaping 
with new landscaping (thus not increasing hardscape within the developed area under the riparian canopy), the 
implementation of BMPs that will be utilized by the project to protect the sensitive riparian habitat and the stream, 
and the lack of any permanent disturbance to any sensitive riparian habitat or areas below TOB, and the full 
avoidance of both applicable City setbacks for the new building, the impacts to riparian habitats from the project 
would be considered less than significant.

SUBJECT:
Signage for Student Pick-up/Drop-off along La Salle Dr
2033 La Salle Dr, San Mateo, CA 94403
PA25-012: The Carey School Early Childhood Education Center
Dear Simin Zakavand:
Public Works has investigated the recommendation made by Planning Commission on the addition of signage 
along La Salle Dr to facilitate The Carey School’s Parking and Traffic Plan. 
San Mateo Municipal Code Section 11.20.010 allows the City Manager exclusive power and duty to place and 
maintain, or cause to be placed and maintained, official traffic control devices when deemed necessary. 
The Parking and Traffic Plan provided for this planning application (PA25-012) is a modified version of what 
was accepted under the previous entitlement for the main campus (PA18-069). The PA18-069 Parking and 
Traffic Plan required no parking along the cul-de-sac during peak hours. There are existing non-conforming 
“No Parking Signs” along the cul-de-sac which was not part of the previous entitlement and have been placed 
without city approval. Through the PA25-012 project entitlement, the developer would be required to remove 
the existing non-conforming signs, and as was the intent per PA18-069, install city standard signs and poles as 
necessary at the designated pick-up/drop-off locations along the cul-de-sac for the peak hours. A template of 
the signage to use can be found in Attachment 1.
Public Works concurs with the Planning Commission and recommends adding a condition of approval stating 
that the developer will be required to implement the appropriate signage on their offsite improvement plans 
and obtain an encroachment permit for installation that must be issued prior to building permit issuance.
Attachment 1 – Sign Template
Sincerely,
John Thompson,
Assistant Engineer

To:
Planning Commission

Joanna Winter; Sung H. Kwon; Zachary Dahl
Subject:
Planning Commission Regular Meeting for 12.9.2025 -The Carey school 
 
Good afternoon Commissioners, 
 
We received the following questions/comments regarding the Carey School Early Childhood Education 
Center on tomorrow’s agenda from one of the Commissioners. Please see the responses below, 
highlighted in blue: 
1. The report says the following about the interplay between SUPs and the actual re-zoning.  As I am 
new to the commission, I'm having a little trouble understanding the interplay between SUPs and 
the zoning.  Could they get approval of this project with just an SUP and without the change in the 
Q8 overlay, or do they require both?  Could you explain how the two interact for me a bit more? 
a. Report: Extending and amending the Q8 Overlay for the Early Childhood Education Center 
maintains consistency with prior Q overlays for private institutions. While educational 
facilities are allowed in One Family Dwellings districts through a Special Use Permit (SUP), 
the proposed zoning reclassiﬁcation and code amendments would facilitate 
implementation of General Plan policies, while ensuring that development standards 
remain compatible with the surrounding residential neighborhood and that regulatory 
oversight is maintained. With the adoption of the proposed overlay, the Project will 
conform to all applicable zoning code standards. Private educational facilities are 
generally allowed in the R1-B zoning district with an SUP. However, an SUP alone still 
requires compliance with the standard R1-B development regulations, which are intended 
for single-family uses. Due to the site conﬁguration and the distance of the oƯ-site parking, 
the project cannot meet those standards and therefore cannot be developed as proposed 
without the Q8 overlay. Rezoning the site to R1-B/Q8 would provide the ﬂexible 
development standards needed to accommodate the proposed layout and oƯ-site parking. 
As a result, both the SUP (to allow the use) and the Q8 overlay (to allow ﬂexible 
development standards) are required for the project. 
 
2. There were resident concerns about the safety of the preschool children.  Do you know what 
existing signage there is (e.g., school zone, slow down signs, etc.)?  Did the city consider adding 
conditions requiring additional signage regarding the school site (other than the daily a frame 
signage discussed in the conditions for use during drop oƯ). The surrounding area has been 
studied through the city 'Slow for Students' program, following California Vehicle Code (CVC) 
22358.4, which posted reduced speed limit signs along 20th Ave, from 25 mph to 15 mph, for this 
studied area under phase 2. La Salle Drive was also evaluated but did not qualify for a reduced 
speed limit. The reduced speed provisions apply only to elementary, middle, or high schools and 
do not apply to the proposed early childhood education center. Additionally, the Local 
329 of 409

--- page 330 ---
2
Transportation Analysis did not recommend any additional signage along La Salle. However, the 
Planning Commission may consider discussing additional signage if they feel it would be 
appropriate. 
 
3. I saw some diƯering information regarding the number of spots reserved at the school for 
students whose seats are subsidized.  One document said 10%, another said 15%.  Do you know 
how many spots will be subsidized? I didn't see these subsidized spots as a condition of approval, 
is that correct?  Is there anything requiring that some number of spots be subsidized? According 
to the applicant, the percentage ranges from 10–15% each year. There is no City requirement to 
subsidize these seats. 
 
4. If I am reading it correctly, the traƯic study says the project (as it concerns traƯic) doesn't qualify 
for the CEQA small project exemption that the City is relying on for the project as a whole, but 
instead qualiﬁes for the Local-service retail and public services exemption.  Could you explain 
whether we disagree with the traƯic consultant about the qualiﬁcation for the small project 
exemption or whether there is a way to reconcile the traƯic study's conclusion that it does not 
apply with our invocation of that exemption?  The CEQA small-structure exemption is 
independent of VMT screening because each evaluates diƯerent factors. The CEQA small-
structure exemption is based on the physical characteristics of the building, such as its square 
footage, while the VMT small-project screening criteria is based on the number of trips the project 
generates. A project may be screened out of VMT analysis under any screening criteria (e.g., low 
trip generation, local-serving retail, aƯordable housing, proximity to transit) and still qualiﬁes for 
CEQA small-structure exemption if it meets the square footage threshold. In this case, since the 
project is less than 10,000 SF in an urbanized area, it meets the CEQA small-structure exemption 
criteria. However, because the VMT small-project screening evaluates the project based on trips 
generated rather than square footage, it does not meet the VMT small-project screening criteria.

Hi Patrick,

Thank you for reaching out. Please note that the project has been recently submitted to the city, and staff
is still conducting the first round of review. The information provided below is based on the initial
application submitted by the applicant and may be updated as we receive additional information and
materials in subsequent submittals.

Please see my responses below in blue:

1.

Can you summarize this process? The request is for a Special Use Permit and a Site Plan and
Architectural Review to demolish the existing single-family residence and accessory dwelling unit
(ADU) on site and construct a new early education center in a residential zoning district. The
criteria and review process for the requested permits includes an application completeness
review and an evaluation of compliance with the Zoning Code, General Plan, and state law
requirements. Additionally, the project will be reviewed in compliance with the California
Environmental Quality Act (CEQA). Staff will review the application materials based on these
requirements and provide comments to the applicant. Once all comments have been addressed,
the project will be scheduled for a public hearing with prior public notification.

Is this process documented online? Yes, the application materials and the latest updates will be

uploaded to the "What’s Happening" page for the project. Please visit this link for the most up-to-
date information. We will continue to update the site as we receive new information from the

333 of 409


--- page 334 ---
applicant. Additionally, | will include you on our interested party list to send you notifications
about future public hearings related to this project.

3. What makes criteria like an environmental study or a traffic impact study necessary? Typically,
project potential impacts trigger environmental studies. In this case, the project will be required
to provide several technical studies, such as traffic, noise, and parking assessments, to
determine the appropriate level of environmental review in accordance with CEQA.

4. How about laws such as SB 9 and statements from City Hall declaring they will do everything to
preserve and increase the number of single-family residences in San Mateo. Does the planning
department get involved in those issues? Yes, staff will evaluate the project in accordance with
state housing laws.

Comments are welcomed throughout the process. If you have additional questions, feel free to reach out
to me.

Thank you,

Simin Zakavand, AICP (She/Her)

Dear Ms. Zakavand and the City of San Mateo Planning Division,

lam writing as a concerned neighbor regarding the proposed project at 2033 La Salle Drive by The
Carey School, as listed on your website here:

https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/4857/2033-La-Salle-Drive-The-Carey-School.

While | understand the importance of early childhood education, | am very concerned about the
conversion of a residential single-family lot into a commercial use, which would reduce much-needed
housing stock in our already tight residential market. The neighborhood is not zoned for large-scale
educational facilities, and this proposal seems misaligned with the current residential character of the
area.

Additional concerns include:

Traffic and Safety: The addition of 75 more students, along with their families, faculty, and staff, will
drastically increase vehicle traffic and congestion during drop-off and pick-up times. This raises
serious safety concerns for pedestrians and residents.

Parking: Street parking is extremely limited, and this project will further reduce available space for local
residents.

July 11, 2025

City of San Mateo

City Councilmembers
Planning Commissioners
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo, CA 94403

Subject: The Carey School Early Childhood Center, 2033 La Salle Drive, San Mateo, CA
Dear Members of the San Mateo Planning Commission and City Council,

We, the undersigned, respectfully submit this petition in support of the proposed preschool
located at 2033 La Salle Drive, in a single-family neighborhood in the City of San Mateo. This
project addresses a critical and well-documented need for quality early childhood education and
care within our community.

Addressing Community Need:

San Mateo and the broader County of San Mateo face a significant shortage of childcare
spaces. Needs assessments consistently demonstrate that demand for quality early education
far exceeds the available supply. This shortage leaves working families with limited options,
often resulting in long waitlists and childcare arrangements that do not meet the developmental
needs of our youngest residents. The proposed preschool seeks to alleviate part of this burden
by providing a nurturing, local option for families, including subsidized care for up to 15% of the
spaces.

Alignment with City Policies:

The City of San Mateo’s General Plan outlines clear policies and goals supporting the

expansion of childcare services within neighborhoods. Promoting local childcare not only aligns
with these policies but also strengthens the community by supporting working families, fostering
early childhood development, and contributing to the overall well-being of San Mateo residents.

Balancing Neighborhood Concerns:

We acknowledge the concerns raised by neighboring homeowners, primarily regarding traffic
and noise. In response, this summer we will be conducting a voluntary traffic study and noise
study to evaluate potential impacts. Furthermore, proactive measures will be implemented to
minimize disruptions, including staggered drop-off and pick-up schedules, designated parking
solutions, and sound-mitigating landscaping and building orientation. We will also have school
staff monitoring 20th and La Salle at drop off and pick up. We believe these measures will
address the valid concerns of residents while allowing the community to benefit from
much-needed childcare services.

school. The school is also planning to invite neighbors to campus in early September to discuss
the project and share findings from the technical studies performed. Email addresses collected
below will be used for invitations to this neighborhood meeting.

Conclusion:

We urge the City to recognize the importance of balancing neighborhood concerns with the
critical need for accessible, quality childcare as outlined in its own General Plan. The proposed
preschool represents a thoughtful, community-focused solution to a documented problem, with
mitigation strategies in place to minimize local impacts.

We respectfully ask for your support of this project to help bridge the childcare gap in San Mateo
and provide families with the resources they need to thrive.

Re: Support for The Carey School Early Childhood Center

Dear Honorable Mayor and City Councilmembers / Planning Commission Chair and Commissioners -
On behalf of First 5 San Mateo County, | am pleased to express our strong support for The Carey
School’s proposed Early Childhood Center in the City of San Mateo.

San Mateo County continues to face a significant shortage of licensed early care and education (ECE)
spaces, particularly for infants, toddlers, and preschool-aged children. This shortage affects families’
ability to work, children’s ability to access high-quality early learning environments, and the stability of our
local economy. First 5 San Mateo County has long prioritized increasing high-quality ECE capacity,
improving access and affordability, and supporting the workforce that makes this essential care possible.
The Carey School’s proposal advances several of these key priorities:

e Creates 75 new high-quality spaces for children ages 2—5 at a time when additional capacity is
critically needed.

e Offers full-day programming (7:45 AM-6:00 PM) that meets the needs of working families
across the county.

e Commits at least 10% of seats to be fully subsidized, expanding equitable access for families
who would otherwise face barriers to high-quality care.

e Invests in a modern, purpose-built facility that supports early learning, family engagement, and
smooth transitions into kindergarten.

These elements reflect the kind of thoughtful, community-responsive expansion that strengthens San
Mateo County’s early childhood system and aligns with the shared goals outlined in the County’s Early
Learning and Care Infrastructure efforts.

We appreciate The Carey School’s commitment to expanding access to early care and education and its
willingness to partner with the community to address one of San Mateo County’s most pressing needs.
We respectfully encourage the City to approve this proposal.

Thank you for your leadership and for your ongoing support of young children and families in San Mateo.

Warm regards,

Kitty Lopez

Executive Director

cc: Payroll Clerk

Re: Support for The Carey School Early Childhood Center

Dear San Mateo City Councilmembers and Planning Commissioners,

We are writing as San Mateo parents of two young children who finally found high-quality,
reliable early childhood care with The Carey School. We are two working parents with two
children, currently at different schools - it’s been such a nightmare to find quality care we can
trust and on top of that logistics is not an easy feat.

This is why we strongly support The Carey School’s proposed Early Childhood Center.

We are counting on The Carey School and its Early Childhood Center for reliable and consistent
care for both our children.

This project would add 75 much-needed child-care spaces for children ages 2—5, with full-day
programming from 7:45 AM to 6:00 PM, exactly the kind of schedule that allows parents to work
without constantly worrying about pickup and coverage with a consolidated drop off and pick up
with the elementary school. As a child that heavily benefited from financial aid myself, I’m also
grateful that the project includes some fully subsidized spots to ensure that more families can
access high-quality early education.

We believe early learning in a neighborhood environment is critical to child development and
community building. We also live next to a school and experience first-hand the traffic
congestion during drop off and pick ups - we understand the stress this might put on some
neighbors. However, we know this is a small price to pay for what the neighborhood schoo!
provides for our children and youth. If we cannot have reliable, great schools right in our
neighborhoods, where would we go? Wouldn’t more driving mean more congestion for our city?

| hope you will support this project and help address one of the most pressing needs facing
families in our city.

Thank you very much for your service and consideration.

With gratitude,
Debbie Limongan & Jeffrey Chung
San Mateo Parent

FROM:
Alex Khojikian, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
January 12, 2026 
SUBJECT:
Solid Waste 2026 Rate Setting and Proposition 218 Notification — Approval
RECOMMENDATION:
Provide direction on proposed increases to residential solid waste rates and authorize staff to mail a Proposition 218 
Notification to all property owners proposing a not to exceed increase in solid waste, recycling, and compost collection 
rates for 2026.
BACKGROUND:
The City’s Solid Waste Program (Program) includes waste diversion, compost/recycling education and outreach, special 
collection events, construction and demolition recycling plan processing, litter reduction programs, illegal dumping 
abatement, and hazardous waste management, and ensures compliance with all county, regional, state, and federal 
regulations. Solid waste, recycling, and organics collection, processing, and disposal services are available to all 
residents and commercial businesses in the City of San Mateo.
 
Each year, Council authorizes the solid waste rates to cover the costs of the collection services provided by Recology San 
Mateo County (Recology); the processing and disposal services provided by South Bayside Industries, Inc. (SBI); the City’s 
portion of the costs of membership in the joint powers authority, South Bayside Waste Management Authority 
(RethinkWaste); and the agency fees, which include the City’s solid waste and street sweeping programs, trash capture 
device maintenance, landfill fee, and franchise fees. The City retains HF&H Consultants (HF&H) to assist in developing a 
rate structure to fund the cost of solid waste services.
 
In 2021, the City adopted a long-term plan for incremental adjustment to the residential solid waste rates to bring them 
into alignment over time with their true cost of service. This is an ongoing effort. 
 
The exclusive franchise agreement between the City and Recology San Mateo County allows for inflationary increases to 
Recology’s collection expenses: fuel costs, labor costs, vehicle maintenance costs, and other costs. Recology’s annual 
compensation increases are reviewed and approved by the Board of Directors of RethinkWaste, of which a City Council 
member sits as a member. The agreement was renewed in 2019 and will expire in 2035.
 
For rate year 2026, the City faces increased costs for collection, processing, and disposal services. 
 
Recology’s collection costs in 2026 increased four percent compared to 2025. After review, the RethinkWaste Board of 
Directors found the proper inflation factors were used to determine Recology’s allowable compensation for 2025 and the 
increases were approved.
 
The processing and disposal services fees set by RethinkWaste are increasing seven percent in 2026. The cost increase is a 
402 of 409

--- page 403 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
result of a five-percent increase to the tipping fee rates set by RethinkWaste and increased material processed at the 
Shoreway Facility.
 
In addition to collection, processing and disposal costs, solid waste rates also fund the City’s street sweeping activities, street 
sweeper vehicle purchases, and trash capture device maintenance and installation. Program costs associated with operating 
the solid waste enterprise are also funded through rates.
 
The 2026 cost increase is also a result of the decision of the City Council last year to defer $331,333 in increased costs 
from 2025 to 2026, as allowed under the franchise agreement. That decision lowered rates in 2025 but must be accounted 
for this year.
Maintaining current rates to meet the 2026 projected expenses described above would lead to an anticipated deficit of 
$1,170,910. Therefore, staff recommends the following step be taken by the City Council to address the revenue shortfall 
for 2025:
 
1.
Authorize raising residential rates by a range of $4.16-$6.50 per month. These increases will result in a deficit of 
$14,137 in 2026. In addition, residential customers subscribing to 96-gallon solid waste carts will meet their cost of 
service.
 
Table A summarizes the current and proposed 2026 residential rates. These rates include collection, processing, and disposal 
of garbage, recycling, and organics.
 
Table A – Proposed 2026 Residential Solid Waste Rate Changes
